(3rd Day Special Dispatch)

Silk Industry Proposes Control Procedures

[Nanjing] The China Silk Improvement Association plans to implement control over the silk industry this year and has decided on the following procedures: 1. Dispatch over forty personnel to various silkworm breeding villages to supervise and guide the use of improved silkworm seeds. 2. Restrict the methods used by silk merchants to collect cocoons. 3. Regulate the price of cocoon collection. 4. Regulate the funds used by cocoon merchants, which will be borrowed from banks on their behalf by the control agency. If any cocoon collectors do not comply with the regulations, the banks will be notified to stop payment. In addition, the control of silk cocoons will also stipulate two items: 1. Pay attention to reducing export costs to facilitate foreign transactions. 2. Improve the output and standardize the machinery of silk reeling factories across the country to ensure uniform quality. The association will allocate 135,240 yuan to supplement the improvement of silk factory machinery. (3rd Day Special Dispatch)

Regarding water conservancy in North China, last year's Yellow River breach caused extensive damage. The provincial government has tried its best to provide relief but is unable to do so. This time, he also plans to consult with relevant parties to obtain a unified solution. Because there are no traces of bandits in the counties of Hebei Province, security is currently very stable. As for construction matters in the province, due to limited financial resources, in addition to the North China Sports Field built in Tianjin before the year and the canal currently being built in Lingshou, which are relatively large in scale, the rest are repairs of rivers and roads. According to the situation last year, Hebei Province's finances had a shortfall of about one million yuan for the year. If this year's harvest is slightly better and some adjustments are made, there should be no problems. Regarding drug prohibition, Hebei Province is currently conducting it strictly. It is reported that Yu is scheduled to visit Chairman Lin and Premier Wang on the 4th to report on everything. (3rd Day Central News Agency Telegram)

Ministry of Industry Discusses Industry Standards

[Nanjing] The Ministry of Industry believes that Article 6 of the Industrial and Commercial Guild Law stipulates that a guild should be established for the same industry in the same region, limited to one guild. Therefore, the same industry in the same region should not have more than one guild. However, industries with slightly different names, such as rice shops and grain shops, often separately organize guilds. According to the regulations of the Merchant Movement Guidance Outline, industries with similar natures and no different businesses should join the same name organization as much as possible. The ministry has specifically proposed discussing an industry standard method with the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee to unify them. (3rd Day Central News Agency Telegram)

Current Commentary

International Perspectives on Loans to China

— Liu

Since the voices for Eastern cooperation have grown louder by the day, Western attention has also deepened. British parliamentarians frequently raise questions, and the U.S. authorities have also made statements. The League of Nations' Council, which was once sought but met with a firm refusal, now seems easily attainable. Truly, "A scholar who has been away for three days must be looked at with new eyes." This is driven by the prevailing trend and vested interests. When matters reach a critical point, they cannot help but come forward with the desire to dip a finger into the pot and get a share. Britain, based on its good intentions to assist China, has proposed to the U.S., France, and Japan to provide financial aid to China. It is said that the U.S. has shown a concrete willingness to cooperate, while Japan seems to express its dissatisfaction. Currently, international competition is unusually complex. How will the situation develop in the future, and how will the powers engage in scheming for their own interests? We need not speculate about that for now. However, how should we receive the good intentions of our friends in the East and West? This is something that we should pay attention to.

I have often said that one must be qualified to borrow money. For example, when the British borrow money from the Americans, there are no other issues besides the terms agreed upon by both parties. However, when the Chinese borrow money from foreigners, the reality is unlikely to be so simple. For example, the Cao Rulin faction's opposition to the Four-Power Consortium loan in 1920 was precisely to supervise our finances and open the door to international co-management. The reason why Eiichi Shibusawa's investment in China in 1916 aroused suspicion was that he wanted to use American money, channeled through the hands of the Japanese, to lend to us, which implied political motives. The situation is certainly different now, but whether the image of China in the eyes of foreigners is the same as what we see and believe about ourselves is a very important question. It is essential to prevent them from reverting to old habits, seeking the power to supervise under the guise of lending, or engaging in the reality of plunder under the name of cooperation. Politics and economics are nominally two but actually one, and they are inseparable.

Furthermore, the use of borrowed funds is also of great importance. If used properly, it can revitalize the country; if used improperly, it can ruin the country. Water can carry a boat, but it can also capsize it. Therefore, the use of borrowed funds should be cautious. In the past, foreign debts were often diverted to political expenses or used to compensate for private losses. This should no longer be the case now. The funds must be used for production and construction, such as currency reform, to lay the foundation for economic revival. This is how borrowing can revitalize the country. However, there are often interferences from creditors when using foreign debts to run industries. First, it is conditional on hiring foreigners. Second, all materials must be purchased from them. Third, if managed properly, it is better than not doing it at all. However, cooperation with foreigners often involves paying huge salaries and only receiving a paper report. Or, due to a lack of understanding of China's national conditions, they may even forcefully implement unfeasible measures, resulting in half the effort and double the results, losing all the essence. It is difficult to say whether this is beneficial or harmful.

Foreigners should also share the blame for creating China's current situation of material scarcity. Foreign goods have long regarded China as their only sales outlet, and their sole purpose has been to extract money from the Chinese. They have destroyed its original productive enterprises without helping it with new construction, leading to the current state of financial exhaustion, where even foreign goods cannot be afforded. This is no different from killing the chicken to get the eggs. For example, the United States absorbs silver, thinking it can increase the price of silver and promote China's purchasing power. However, China's silver has long been exhausted from purchasing foreign goods. Even if there is any left, it is mostly silver in the vaults of foreign banks. Seeing the opportunity for profit, they disregard the dangers of the Chinese market and ship it out in droves, creating China's current situation of extreme austerity. Therefore, if the Chinese were truly rich in silver, the American approach would not be a bad one. Unfortunately, the Chinese are exhausted. Although silver is expensive and American goods are cheap, most people still have to look at them and walk away. The United States has gained little, but the harm it has done to China is significant. Therefore, if foreigners truly want to help China, they should abandon their extractive policies and consider the difficulties China is currently facing, reducing the factors that could increase its difficulties. On one hand, they should genuinely support production and construction that meet China's needs to increase the productivity of the Chinese people, which will increase their purchasing power for foreign goods. However, foreigners do not see this far. They only care about immediate interests, competing with each other and leaving no room for future development. If future loans to China are still about seizing power and extracting profits, it will not benefit China, nor will it benefit foreigners.

Sun Yat-sen once strongly advocated the international joint development of Chinese industries. His hopes for countries investing were: "(1) The governments investing must act together, unify policies, and form an international group. Use their organization, management talents, and skilled technicians to design in a systematic way and use materials accurately to avoid waste and facilitate work. (2) They must gain the trust of the Chinese people so that they enthusiastically help this endeavor. (3) That is, hold formal meetings with the Chinese government to discuss the final contract of this plan." In this way, "China can open a new market, which can sell its own products and also sell foreign products without interfering with each other." Although Sun Yat-sen's proposal was made more than a decade ago, it is still a principle that China should adhere to today. If productive enterprises can truly develop, then why would China's finances need assistance? There is always a solution. As for currency reform, it is also a form of construction and does not need to be discussed separately. We do not want to comment too much before it becomes a reality. What has been said above is merely expressing our views for the reference of our compatriots.

Proclamation of Abdication by the King of Siam Published

The Content and Wording are Very Simple

No Mention of Succession to the Throne

[London] King Prajadhipok of Siam formally announced his abdication today at his residence in Surrey, near London. His abdication proclamation was signed at 1:45 PM on the 2nd, and shortly afterwards, it was forwarded to the Speaker of the National Assembly of Siam by the Siamese Legation in Britain. The full text of the proclamation was released to the newspapers this morning by the King's Private Secretary. Its candor and simplicity of wording are rarely seen in abdication proclamations of emperors. The proclamation was typed on four pages, signed only by the King, and will be officially announced in Siam. The content informs the people of Siam about the general situation since the coup of June 24, 1932, expressing the King's deep desire to establish a constitutional government and his willingness to adhere to democratic principles. However, the conditions for his restoration, which he presented to the National Assembly, were rejected. Therefore, he had no choice but to abdicate immediately. The proclamation does not mention who will succeed the King after his abdication. (3rd, Havas Dispatch)

[London] The King's Secretary stated to reporters that the abdication document consists of four pages and has been signed by the King, and will be officially announced in Siam. It mentions the conditions for restoration that were previously proposed. These conditions are based entirely on genuine democratic principles, including: (1) freedom of speech, (2) freedom of assembly for political parties, (3) the inclusion of provisions in the criminal law to protect the constitution, with political prisoners tried by ordinary courts, (4) amnesty for political prisoners, (5) the restoration of officials dismissed on suspicion of political activity to their original positions, and (6) the prohibition of active military and naval officers from participating in politics. The Secretary also stated that after his abdication, the King will use the title of Prince Sukhothai and travel to various places. He will temporarily remain in Britain until June of this year to settle various matters, and then he may reside in Switzerland. (3rd, Reuters Dispatch)

[London] The King of Siam signed his abdication document today. The King has repeatedly sought to abdicate because the Siamese Parliament restricts his power. Last year, representatives from Bangkok were sent to persuade him to retract his abdication intention. At that time, the King was still hesitant, but later hinted at letting another prince of the royal family succeed him. According to those familiar with Siamese affairs, if the King retires, the successor will be his eleven-year-old nephew, Mahidol, who currently resides in Lausanne, Switzerland. At that time, Siam will form a regency council to assist him in ruling Siam. (3rd, National Telegram)

Japan and Siam to Adopt Cooperative Air Force Policy

Air Routes Between the Two Countries Are Being Planned

[Tokyo] Since Siam's withdrawal from the League of Nations, friendship between Japan and Siam has become increasingly close. Japan has agreed to provide special training to the Siamese Navy and has sent many naval instructors and aviation instructors to Siam. This summer, Siamese aviators will come to Japan. Japan plans to send a squadron of naval aircraft to Siam within this year for aviation festivities. The airship route between Tokyo and Bangkok is also being actively planned. China United Press, Bangkok: It has recently been learned that a certain Japanese merchant has specially sent representatives to Siam to search for and purchase scrap iron. With such a huge demand, the market price of scrap iron in Siam will definitely improve. As for what the iron is purchased for, it is not known to outsiders.

1934 Was the Worst Year for American Youth

Moral Decline Reached Its Peak

The Ruin of Humanity Was Shocking

World News Agency, New York: Mr. Drake, Secretary-General of the YMCA in New York, stated in his 1934 annual report that this year was one of the worst in American history for American youth because they felt "unneeded in the world." He continued, "The full extent of the tragedy and evil of these young people may never be known, because the decline of the spiritual and moral qualities is subtle and invisible, difficult to quantify. Sacred scars are not revealed on the sleeves. However, the ruin of humanity is shocking, which is a fact." He also said, "This moral decline is the result of young people spending their youth in a war-torn world, followed by world reconstruction, unhealthy prosperity, and depression. But even if young people are reckless and irresponsible, we cannot but accept a large part of the blame. We must quickly seek remedies to avoid regrets. Although we are in this dark atmosphere, we can still hope that misfortune has reached its peak and that things will improve in the future."

[Nanjing] The U.S. Embassy inquired of our Ministry of Foreign Affairs whether it issues hunting licenses valid nationwide. The Ministry inquired the Ministry of Industry for an interpretation as to whether license holders could hunt throughout the country. The Ministry of Industry replied that the licenses held by people of treaty countries are Class B licenses. According to Article 8 of the Implementing Regulations of the Hunting Law, the Class B hunting licenses issued by the Provincial Departments of Industry should first be sent to the local authorities in the hunting area to solicit their opinions. Anglo-American Cooperation to Aid China Difficult to Implement Currently

Advocate Joint Implementation by Allied French and Italian Countries

Impossible for Japan to Completely Control China

[Washington] After Undersecretary of State Phillips met with British Ambassador Lindsay, he considered Lindsay's proposal for the United States and Britain to independently provide financial assistance to China to be in conflict with the Washington Nine-Power Treaty and the 1920 International Banking Consortium agreement, making it difficult to implement. As far as the U.S. government is concerned, there is no possibility of assisting China at present. Lindsay immediately stated that if the United States and Britain disregard China, they would almost be entrusting China to Japan and allowing it to dominate. Phillips replied that China has a vast territory, and it is unknown how much difficulty Japan would encounter if it wanted to completely control it. As for the United States cooperating with Britain, France, Italy, and other related countries to assist China, it is not impossible. (2nd, Havas Dispatch)

US Refuses to Comment

[Washington] Undersecretary of State Phillips today refused to comment on reports from London that Britain would invite France, Japan, and the United States to explore the possibility of jointly providing financial assistance to China. At the same time, Phillips declined to say whether Britain was the initiator of this proposal. Phillips met with British Ambassador Lindsay yesterday to discuss the possibility of financial assistance to China. (2nd, Reuters Dispatch)

Britain Hopes for Joint Investment

[London] People in authority of the British and American governments are discussing the matter of jointly assisting the Chinese economy in Washington. Well-informed financial circles here hold the following views: Britain has no intention of preventing Japan from providing financial assistance to China. If Japan intends to implement assistance to China alone, this adventurous behavior is not impossible. However, Britain has always hoped that, in addition to Japan, Britain, the United States, and France would jointly implement assistance to China. (2nd, Domei Dispatch)

Anglo-American Relations Drawing Closer

[Washington] The talk of Sino-Japanese amity has clearly brought about a combination of common interests in the Far East between Britain and the United States. Observers believe that although the news from Shanghai has not been confirmed, it is enough to make Downing Street and the State Department eliminate their differences. During President Hoover's time, former Secretary of State Stimson tried to restrict Japan's actions in Manchuria, but Britain failed to fully cooperate with the United States at that time. Currently, the United States also has difficulties because the Senate is quite disobedient to the President on domestic issues, which affects the government's handling of Far East issues. It is said that the simplest solution to China's current financial difficulties is to relax the U.S. silver purchase policy so that the price of silver no longer rises. However, the government is unable to implement this move due to the powerful silver faction in Congress. Although the Treasury Department has recently stopped directly purchasing silver in China, most of what is purchased in London is still Chinese silver shipped from Shanghai last fall. Silver experts here believe that the Treasury Department is buying newly mined silver within its possible range to avoid excessively absorbing silver in the Far East. However, in any case, the U.S. absorption of silver will cause silver prices to rise, and China will be affected. The government may be willing to reduce the amount of silver purchased, but if so, Congress may take drastic measures and pass mandatory resolutions, making it impossible for the Treasury Department to implement its current cautious approach. (2nd, National Telegram)

After the Rebellion is Quelled, the Greek Government is Under Strict Guard

It is said that a Part of the Rebels Retreated to the Island of Kydonies

Those Arrested Will be Tried by a Military Tribunal

Athens: The warships occupied by the rebels have already sailed to the port of Lagonisi on the island of Kydonies. Order on the island is normal, but the situation is not very clear. No clear news has been received here so far. The actual situation on the island should be clear today. The Minister of the Navy, Chatzi-Kyriakos, has recently resigned and been succeeded by Admiral Dousmanis. General Metaxas has been appointed as a minister without portfolio, and the Deputy Minister of Aviation has been promoted. According to the Athens News Agency, the partial reorganization of the cabinet is intended to consolidate its position, as Doumes and Metaxas have long been known for their prestige and will be able to calm the people. As for the attitude of former Prime Minister Venizelos, it is still a concern for the general public. The newspapers run by Venizelos and the newspapers belonging to the opposition party were not published this morning. The non-partisan Esbia newspaper asked the leaders of the opposition party to inform Venizelos of the real situation in the capital, so as not to act rashly. Martial law has now been declared throughout Greece. (Havas telegram, 3rd)

[Paris] The newspapers here have published very detailed news about the Greek incident. Le Journal reported that the governor of Kydonies Island has been silent so far, and the island may have been occupied by the rebels. According to news obtained by L'Echo de Paris, the Greek government has dissolved the Senate because the Venizelos party has a majority in the Senate. In addition, a number of members of parliament belonging to the Venizelos faction have been arrested in Athens. (Havas telegram, 3rd)

The Course of Events in Quelling the Turmoil

Athens: The purpose of this incident was to restore former Prime Minister Venizelos to power. The government authorities had long been aware of this, so they were prepared at any time, and were able to quickly quell the turmoil. According to a statement issued by the authorities, the government had long suspected that some naval and army officers belonging to the Venizelos party, following the orders of General Plastiras, who was in exile overseas, were plotting a rebellion. Martial law is still in force, and the government is able to control the overall situation and prevent further incidents. A small number of rebels who escaped and boarded the cruiser Averoff, the cruiser Helli, and two destroyers are expected to surrender within 24 hours. This uprising was well organized and broke out in several places at the same time. Fifteen officers, following the orders of General Plastiras, entered the Efthymiou Barracks here and persuaded the troops to join the rebellion in front of the regular officers. After this army was confused and disobeyed the ultimatum to surrender, the unmutinied troops shelled their barracks. By dawn yesterday, the crowd surrendered, with three dead and twelve wounded. On Friday, the partisans attempted to occupy the Evelpidon Military Academy without success. Twelve officers led a hundred civilians into the school, detained the principal, and were trying to persuade the cadets to join the rebellion when the government troops arrived and drove them out. The same scene was played at the Perama Arsenal on the island of Crete. Rear Admiral Themistoklis led twenty-five active and reserve naval officers to launch an uprising in cars on Friday evening. The loyal officers of the cruiser Averoff had been tricked into landing in advance, and then the rebels boarded the ship and occupied it. The officers who resisted on the ship were detained. After the rebels occupied the ship, they were able to command the light cruiser Helli and three destroyers and three submarines. Therefore, the government artillery rushed to Perama and began bombarding the rebel ships at one o'clock yesterday morning, but because the distance was too far, they could not hit them. The cannons of the two cruisers were able to hit the town, so the houses in Perama were severely damaged. At four o'clock this morning, the rebel ships had sailed to the northeast end of Crete. Before leaving, the engines and gun positions of the three submarines and one destroyer had been dismantled, so these three ships and one destroyer were still docked in their original locations. The government sent several aircraft to attack the rebel ships. All the planes concentrated their bombardment on the Averoff, so the ship was hit by several bombs and suffered heavy damage. However, two planes were also hit by the ship's anti-aircraft guns, but fortunately they flew back to base safely. After the rebels occupied the warship, Rear Admiral Typaldos mediated. The rebels asked for half an hour to decide on their position. Half an hour later, they declared that they were unwilling to negotiate with the government and sailed away. Although the authorities strictly prohibited gatherings during the period of martial law, a mass rally was still held yesterday afternoon to oppose the revolution. The capital is now calm, with troops carrying rifles and machine guns stationed at various key points. However, public buses have stopped running, and all entertainment venues have been ordered to temporarily suspend business by the police. The newspapers of the opposition party have been banned from publication, and letters and telegrams are strictly checked. (Reuters telegram, 3rd)

Former Prime Minister Admits Involvement

Athens: Former Prime Minister Venizelos, who is currently residing on the island of Crete, today formally admitted that he was of one mind with the rebels who attempted to overthrow the government yesterday. The government has ordered a curfew from 10:00 p.m. to the next morning, and has organized a military tribunal to try the arrested rebels. The government has decided that if the rebel ships do not surrender by tomorrow, it plans to bombard them fiercely with the Greek Air Force. There are currently three bombers, fully loaded with bombs weighing 200 pounds each, waiting for orders to depart. According to the commander of the air force, the cruiser Averoff fired a hundred times at the planes yesterday, but none hit. The rebel ships also fought the planes with machine guns. General Plastiras, who is currently residing in Cannes, denies any involvement in this rebellion. Today, he told a Reuters reporter that he knew nothing about the domestic turmoil except for reading the newspapers. He also said that he did not want to leave France at the moment, and that the recent developments in Greece were not surprising, as he believed that half of the country opposed the current government. (Reuters telegram, 3rd)

British Government Invites Former Prime Minister Lloyd George to Join the Cabinet

[London] The move by the National Government to invite former Prime Minister Lloyd George, the leader of the Liberal opposition party, to come out of the mountains and cooperate has been regarded as interesting by political and parliamentary circles, and has been commented on one after another. In the past three months, Lloyd George has expressed fierce opposition to the chaos of the economy, finance, and society, and has advocated the adoption of a controlled economy to remedy it. Although the proposed plan is large in scale, it is also too broad. The National Government has invited him to join the cabinet at this time to show respect and to urge him to try his hand and not to be satisfied with passive opposition. As for Lloyd George, he replied that he opposed all the government's current work, and that the effective measures for economic recovery were not limited to those proposed by individuals. All those who are helpful to this undertaking, no matter where they come from, should be considered. The best way is to organize a parliamentary committee to conduct research. (Havas telegram, 2nd)

Lloyd George Writes an Article Advocating British-American Cooperation

[London] Liberal Party leader Lloyd George, who was the British Prime Minister during the European War, published an article in the Weekly Illustrated, stating the absolute necessity of maintaining a common policy between Britain and the United States in dealing with the Far Eastern question. George recalled the commercial reflections of the spread of Japanese power throughout Asia, saying that once China was under Japanese command, the open door would never exist, and the valuable Chinese market would be lost forever. We should aim to obtain a Far Eastern solution that takes into account the best interests of China, Japan, Britain, and the United States. Neither Britain nor the United States can hope to achieve any success alone in achieving this goal, but if Britain and the United States cooperate, they can guarantee that the development of China and Japan will become a harmonious factor in world progress. Simon Eden to Arrive in Berlin on the 7th of Next Month

The German Government Plans to Treat Him as a Guest of Honor

There is a Saying that the Trip to Moscow Will be Postponed

[Paris] According to news from London received by Le Matin, British Foreign Secretary Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden are scheduled to arrive in Berlin on the evening of the 7th, i.e., Thursday, and hold talks with Chancellor Hitler on Friday and Saturday. Japanese-Puppet Regime Expansion of Air Transport Plans

Eager to Link Japan, Korea, Soviet Russia, and Puppet Organizations by Air

Harbin Dispatch: In order to strengthen its air force and expand its transportation business, Japan is now actively promoting an expansion of its air transport plans through the Ministry of Railways. This air transport will be managed by the Ministry of Railways and will not be related to the Japan Air Transport Company. The principle is "Safety First," using the world's best aircraft. Overseas offices have already been instructed to investigate the achievements of air transport operated by railways in the UK, the US, and Germany. At the same time, in addition to expanding the "Manchurian Aviation Network," regular passenger transport, and air postal services, which are already completed, it has recently instigated the puppet organization to start negotiations with the Soviet Union, hoping to realize Eurasian intermodal transport. This matter was raised when Ito, a postal affairs official of the Harbin Postal Administration, visited European countries in 1933 to introduce the puppet state's postal services, but no response was received from the Soviet side. This time, the puppet organization's Ministry of Communications, taking the view that postal services are a product of human welfare, wants to negotiate with the Soviet Union again, hoping to reach an agreement. The Soviet Union's regular aviation is operated by the state, with air routes between Moscow, Chita, and Vladivostok. The Japanese-puppet regime's plan is to extend the Soviet regular air route from Chita to Bolshaya Ulya along the Zabaikalsk Railway line, and hopes to implement air intermodal transport and exchange mail between Manchuria and Bolshaya Ulya. If this connection is realized, mail from Tokyo to Moscow, which previously took four weeks, can be delivered in just one week, opening a new era of change in Eurasian air transport connections. Chairman Chiang Goes to Sichuan to Supervise the Suppression of Red Bandits

Optimistic Outlook for the Total Collapse of the Red Bandits

Kong Xiangxi, Song Ziwen, Zhang Xueliang, He Chengjun, Zhang Qun, and Ye Peng all came to the airport to see him off. Madam Chiang Soong Mei-ling took the Yong Sui warship west. Wangcangba is a strategic point in Nanjiang, defending it to secure their old base. Xiaochangba connects to Bikou and Qingchuan, occupying it to plan other escapes. The bandit's previous front line was from east to west, but now it has changed to from south to north.
