Sichuan Province Suspends Advance Collection of Land Taxes

Liu Xiang Telegraphed That Land Taxes Will Be Collected Once a Year

Goods Passing After One-Time Tax Payment Without Obstruction

All Excessive and Miscellaneous Taxes Completely Eliminated

Nanjing Dispatch: The Sichuan Provincial Government Office in Nanjing recently received two telegrams from Chairman Liu's secretariat to the county magistrates, collection bureau chiefs, and the people of Sichuan, formally announcing that from 1935 onwards, land taxes in Sichuan will be collected once a year. During the bandit suppression period, a temporary military fee will be attached to the land tax amount once, and no other collections will be allowed. As for goods, after paying taxes once, they will not be taxed again anywhere in Sichuan, regardless of where they are transported. This is the first major policy of the provincial government after its establishment and is expected by people across the country. The original telegrams are recorded below:

Telegram 1

To all county magistrates and collection bureau chiefs in Sichuan: Our country is based on agriculture, and land taxes are collected once a year, meaning that agricultural land and tax revenue should correspond. During peaceful times in the past, the principle of never increasing taxes was always followed. Unfortunately, Sichuan has frequent military affairs, and the needs are vast, resulting in advances and pre-collection, which has become a habit, causing suffering to our people, which is a constant source of remorse. This chairman has been entrusted with a difficult task, originally hoping to start anew with the people. Land taxes should be restored to the old system, but the bandit atmosphere has not been quelled, and military affairs are ongoing. If the people are to enjoy their work, they must first live in peace. However, if we try to reduce taxes and get closer to the people, it will greatly affect the military. Therefore, based on the principle of choosing the lesser of two evils, we have decided on a policy of gradual improvement. It is now decided by the provincial government meeting that land taxes in all counties of Sichuan will be collected once a year from 1935 onwards. Before the military is reorganized, a temporary military fee will be attached to the annual land tax amount, and no other advances or pre-collections will be allowed. As for the time and procedures, the collection bureaus should carefully consider the local situation, strive for simplicity, and prevent disturbances. Once the bandit troubles are eliminated and the troops are reorganized, it will be stopped immediately. I hope that all the elders and brothers of Sichuan will share the difficulties, strive to relieve the local difficulties, understand the government's difficult situation of considering all aspects, know the seriousness of the mission of the times, endure temporary pain, and plan for permanent peace and tranquility. After this regulation, all collection personnel must be honest and upright. If there are any violations of the law, tricks, or self-interest, once the government finds out, or the people report and it is verified, they will be punished according to the law and will not be tolerated. In addition to sending telegrams separately, the county and bureau should immediately comply and post notices to inform the public, showing the government's concern for the people's suffering, and report the compliance situation for future reference. Liu Xiang, Chairman of the Provincial Government, East (1st day)

Telegram 2

Tax revenue principles should be fair and universal, and the tax system must be unified in order to protect production and cultivate tax sources. In Sichuan, there are many tax revenue items in each county, and numerous bureaus and checkpoints. Merchants and traders are obstructed and detained, and officials exploit and harm them, resulting in a decline in all industries and widespread hardship. If we do not make efforts to rectify this, how can we save the people's livelihood? This chairman was ordered to reorganize the provincial government and deeply considers the state of the market and cherishes the concerns of the merchants. Therefore, after a meeting, it was decided to simplify the various county taxes and set up local tax bureaus. All merchant goods, after paying taxes once, will not be taxed again anywhere in Sichuan, regardless of where they are transported. In addition, all old excessive and miscellaneous taxes will be abolished to avoid disturbances. In addition to determining the tax rules, another order will be issued for implementation. The compliance situation should be reported. Liu Xiang, Chairman of the Provincial Government, East (1st day)

Financial Situation of Shanxi Province

The Provincial Bank's Business Improves

Taiyuan Dispatch: The financial situation in Shanxi Province, since Yan Xishan used his authority as the military governor and provincial governor to expand the scope of the Shanxi Official Money Bureau and reorganize it into the Shanxi Provincial Bank in 1917-18, all public funds in the province have been exclusively managed by the bank. Since then, the financial power of Shanxi Province has been concentrated in the bank. By 1930, the bank's banknotes had been issued to more than 60 million yuan. At that time, except for a small amount of silver dollars circulating in the southern part of Shanxi, most counties in the province relied on provincial banknotes for turnover. Later, due to political changes and the provincial bank's depleted reserve, the price of provincial banknotes plummeted again and again, and the people were miserable. When Yan Xishan returned to power again, he stipulated that 20 yuan of provincial banknotes could be exchanged for one silver dollar, and then cleaned up the mess, started anew, and reissued new banknotes for circulation. In the past three years, although the financial situation of the province seems to have gradually recovered, the vitality has been greatly damaged and cannot be recovered in a short period of time. In recent years, many new banks and money houses have been added in Taiyuan, but most of them are public enterprises run by the government. If the silver houses and money shops organized by the business community, they have all suffered a setback and are in a state of decline. It is found that the silver houses and money shops organized by the business community are mostly reorganized from the old exchange houses, which were also a special skill of the Shanxi people in the past. During the prosperous period of 1930, there were more than 60 such businesses in Taiyuan alone, and they were all thriving and profitable. In the past one or two years, they have closed down one after another, and more than half of them have already closed. Even those that remain are barely maintaining the status quo. The Bank of China used to have a branch in Taiyuan, facing off against the Shanxi Provincial Bank. Later, due to poor business, it was changed to a sub-branch, and then changed to an office. In fact, it is just a matter of maintaining appearances. In addition to the Shanxi Provincial Bank, there are still several public silver and money businesses, such as the Suixi Reclamation Bank, the Railway Bank, and the Jinbei Salt Industry Bank. In recent years, the provincial bank has been reorganized by the bank manager Zhi Xiang, and it made a profit of more than 400,000 yuan last year. If it can continue to work hard and not be affected by political affairs, then the future business has a good prospect for development. However, Wang Xiang has been ordered by the central government to be transferred to the director of the Department of Construction. The position of general manager of the provincial bank that he left behind is being sought by the authorities. The internal affairs of the bank are temporarily maintained by the manager Fu Jianxi. Wang reported to the authorities in detail about the bank's design, business and expenses last year. Because the rise and fall of the provincial bank is very important to the overall financial situation of Shanxi Province, the report is attached as follows:

Design Aspects

(A) Domestic: When the bank was reorganized in 1932, due to environmental and financial reasons, nine domestic branches were abolished. Now, the credit has gradually recovered, and the capital has been changed from 66 million yuan to 12 million yuan according to the actual needs of economic construction. 100,000 yuan will be allocated every month, and it has been allocated on a monthly basis since July last year. In order to regulate the financial situation of the province, it is advisable to set up branches, so that the province's financial networks can be gradually connected. However, setting up branches all over the province will result in huge expenses, which will inevitably be unaffordable. Therefore, we have followed the example of the Bank of China and set up more consignment shops and fewer branches. In fact, it can achieve considerable results, and in terms of expenses, it can avoid unnecessary expenses. Proceeding in this way seems to be more beneficial and less harmful. Therefore, last year, the Tianjin branch was changed to a consignment shop, the Fancun office had simple affairs and was merged into Taigu, and Kelan, Hequ, Xixian, and Lishi were all changed to consignment shops, and more staff were sent to carry out the work. In addition, three consignment shops were added in Wenshui, Jiexiu, and Shouyang, and it is planned to add more consignment shops this year in places with slightly more commercial activity, in order to achieve the goal of universal coverage. (B) Foreign: Exchange is the most important part of banking business. Since the reorganization of the bank, only two foreign business offices have been retained in Tianjin and Suiyuan. It is often felt that the exchange and transportation of goods to major commercial ports outside the province are stagnant and difficult to communicate. It is also an important task for the bank to act as an agent for the treasury and collect public funds from various counties. Wang believes that if a flexible method of exchange is not properly planned, it will not only be inconvenient to use, but also the transportation costs will be a waste. The source of hard currency in the province is examined. In addition to the border counties exchanging food, coal, and local products for goods from other provinces, most of them are exchanged for cotton and salt from southern Shanxi and transported into the province. The bank and various money merchants then transfer them from southern Shanxi to the province, and counties near Taiyuan also transfer them out of the province due to transaction needs. Therefore, the bank's annual transportation cost of cash is often no less than 20,000 to 30,000 yuan. Since the Longhai Railway directly connects to Xi'an and the port of Lianyungang has been built, the commercial trend in southern Shanxi is likely to break away from Tianjin and move towards Shaanxi, Zhengzhou, Shanghai, and Wuhan. In the future, business operations must focus on Shaanxi, Zhengzhou, Shanghai, and Wuhan. Therefore, staff were sent to Shaanxi, Henan, Shanghai, and Wuhan for investigation, and it is planned to select appropriate personnel to set up offices in various places to promote development. With such a change, the need for hard currency will be reduced, the transportation expenses will also be reduced, the exchange will be smooth, the business will improve day by day, and the atmosphere of the market will also change.

Business Situation

The bank is a public enterprise, and its articles of association state that its purpose is to regulate the financial situation of the province and support economic construction. Its nature is different from that of ordinary banks, so its business policy must be based on social benefits. All economic construction and public and private industries, if they have value for support, will be assisted to the best of their ability. As for enriching the internal and consolidating the foundation, it is the focus of attention on weekdays. Only with a solid foundation and a rich internal can we deal with the run on the bank in June last year with a calm attitude and try our best to pay in cash. As a result, it was quelled in three days. Since then, the bank's credit has been evident in society, and the efficiency of issuance has been smoother. Not only are the general merchants and people happy to use it, but the post office and railways also accept it and use it in the same way. According to the amount issued at the time of the run, it was more than 4 million yuan. As of the end of the year before the year, it reached more than 5.8 million yuan, which is enough to show that the bank's value has risen, and the public's belief in it has become more widespread. In the future, the internal will be further enriched, and the foundation will be more consolidated in the future. According to the total net profit last year was 426,203 yuan, 6 jiao and 9 fen. After deducting and allocating according to the regulations, and removing more than 30,000 yuan, the net profit was 358,085 yuan, 3 jiao and 3 fen, which is an increase of 119,901 yuan, 9 jiao and 1 fen compared with the previous year. In today's rural bankruptcy and economic depression, it is truly commendable to have such a result.

Actual Expenses

After the reorganization of the bank, the monthly expenses were set at 19,564 yuan. According to the needs of the expenses at that time, it was the lowest limit. Last year, in response to the needs of the social environment, the scope of business has expanded. There are now nine branches, nine offices, nine consignment shops, and 29 agents. As the business is busy, the expenses must be high. However, the annual settlement not only did not exceed the budget, but also saved 21,149 yuan, 5 jiao and 4 fen, which is due to the diligence of the bank's colleagues, the thrift in spending, and the effectiveness of promoting local products and implementing the new life. (February 22)

Page 9

Reorganization of Navigation Administration in Hubei Province

Report from the Construction Department's Navigation Administration Office

Hankou Communication: A one-year report from the Navigation Administration Office of the Construction Department of the Provincial Government, which has been managing inland waterway shipping, is as follows:

"Inland waterway shipping began on a trial basis in February of last year and was officially taken over on March 1st, making today exactly one year. The complexity of the work, the seriousness of its significance, and the enormity of its responsibility have made me, with my shallow knowledge and having studied electrical engineering, and not understanding the specialized knowledge of maritime transport, feel truly ashamed of my incompetence. If a suitable candidate had been found earlier, the results would surely have been ten times greater than they are today. Fortunately, I have been instructed by the Chairman of the Committee, the Chairman, the Director, and the Secretary, and I have also received the support of my colleagues in the department and all the staff in the office, who have worked together with a spirit of struggle to overcome great difficulties. In the past year, we have not encountered any unexpected major changes, and shipping merchants have also been able to enjoy huge profits, and the public has also been able to benefit from reduced prices. We dare not take credit for this, but only express our sincere gratitude.

The current state of shipping is very simple and can be reported with numbers. There are a total of sixty-seven ships under management and fifteen ships leased. According to the machinery, there are sixty-three steamships and nineteen diesel ships. According to the hull, there are nine steel ships and seventy-three wooden hulls. According to size, there is one ship over ten fathoms long, sixteen ships over nine fathoms, and twenty-seven ships over eight fathoms. The total displacement tonnage is approximately 5,900 tons. According to age, there are zero ships built within one year, three ships within two years, sixteen ships within three years, and sixty-three ships older than three years. From these figures, it can be clearly seen that its foundation is not sound. The total displacement is only 6,000 tons, which is less than twice the 3,693 tons of displacement of the China Merchants Bureau's Jianghua, and even less comparable to the 20,000 tons of the Canadian Empress that travels between the United States and China. Compared to the British Queen Mary, which was recently launched and has a displacement of 73,000 tons, it is twelve times smaller. The total estimated value of all inland waterway ships is only 750,000 yuan, which is less than half the cost of one of the China Merchants Bureau's newly built Sihai ships. The cost of the Haiyuan is 1.4 million yuan. It is pitiful that we have to use these dilapidated things to maintain the 1,500-kilometer navigation lines of the entire province's inland waters, and at the beginning of the takeover, it caused a huge uproar. It can be seen that the level of backwardness of our country's production is unbelievable. There are currently twenty-one shipping routes. The Hankou-Caidian route runs four times a day, the Hankou-Yangluo route runs twice a day, and the Hankou-Tuanfeng, Wuxue, Echeng, Huangshigang, Gedian, Cangzibu, Pengjiachang, Xindi, Jinkou, Huanglingji, X溝, Shayang routes, as well as the Shashi-Yichang, Shashi-Ouchi, Shashi-Hao穴, and X溝-Changjiangbu routes, each run once a day. The Hankou-Zhuhe and Maojiakou routes run every other day, and the Hankou-Ouchi route runs three times a week. Strict adherence to schedules and uniform fares have been widely publicized. An average of approximately 6,800 people travel by ship each day.

Shipping revenue and expenditure are settled monthly. The total revenue from mid-February to the end of June was 211,612.60 yuan, and the total expenditure was 187,239.71 yuan, resulting in a surplus of 24,372.89 yuan. The distribution method for the surplus is as follows: half is distributed to shipowners as a bonus at an annual interest rate of eight percent, plus an official interest rate of eight percent, for a total of one point six percent. The total revenue for the second half of the year, from July to the end of December, was 600,476.05 yuan, and the expenditure was 430,119.62 yuan, leaving a balance of 180,356.43 yuan. All official interest and repair depreciation expenses have been paid. However, one-third of the ships have not been overhauled due to time constraints. Therefore, it was decided to first withdraw 40,000 yuan from the above balance for repair costs to overhaul the ships, and then withdraw 5,000 yuan for public welfare funds. The remaining amount will be distributed to shipping merchants as a bonus, calculated based on the estimated value of the ship's capital, reaching an annual interest rate of two point three percent, plus an official interest rate of eight percent, for a total of three point one percent, which can be said to be the highest in Wuhan's industries. Compared to the official interest rate of eight percent and the bonus of eight percent, for a total of one point six percent, at the end of June last year, it has doubled. The above official interest is paid monthly, and the second-half bonus will also be paid in two installments before the end of the lunar year, with the remaining amount to be paid off by the end of this month. In addition, depreciation, calculated at seven percent for steel ships and one percent for wooden ships, is also paid monthly based on the number of days each ship operates. Therefore, shipowners benefit by about four percent. The remaining half of the surplus, 10,186.45 yuan for the first half of the year and 67,678.22 yuan for the second half of the year, totaling 77,864.67 yuan, will be used to reorganize the shipping routes, according to the plan. The purchase of dredging machines to dredge waterways and the construction of water gates are all in the design phase. At yesterday's provincial government meeting, it was discussed that the total of official interest and bonuses was three point one percent, which exceeded the two point five percent interest rate limit stipulated in the Public Utilities Supervision Regulations. However, in order to be considerate of shipping merchants and maintain the government's credibility, it was decided to pay the full amount according to the plan. But are the shipowners satisfied with one point six percent in the first half of the year and three point one percent in the second half of the year? No, the Chinese will never be satisfied. If they are not satisfied with the business, they will strive to expand it, which is a good thing. Unfortunately, most people are not satisfied with monetary benefits. This further proves that the profits that shipping merchants claimed to have lost a year ago were probably no less than one hundred percent. How can the shipping industry be compared to other industries in the country?

We have been trying out inland navigation for a year, and due to various reasons such as manpower and equipment, nine out of ten things have not been done well. The most painful thing is the lack of cooperation from shipping merchants. We are moving forward with a spirit of struggle and fearlessness, ignoring all kinds of alienation and sabotage, and taking great risks. For example, at the beginning of March last year, all the ships fled to Jiujiang. Except for maintaining the routes with six small ships, we were ordered to go to Qizhou to escort back the fleeing ships. The Hanxing ship we were on collided with the Mingguang ship of the Shihuiyao and Asia Oil Company at night, causing huge holes in the hulls of both ships, only two inches above the waterline. Fortunately, both sides were empty, otherwise water would have entered the cabins and there would have been sacrifices. We were thinking about the business, but they did not know it. Therefore, all kinds of difficulties can be broken. Other difficulties can be briefly reported in several items.

Seafarers are the basic talent of the shipping industry. The rise and fall, survival and death of the shipping industry are really shared with the seafarers. However, there are some non-deck and bottom seafarers who, under the name of seafarers, wantonly make requests. The cabin boy system in the middle cabin of large ships is still preserved, but we have broken it. From the beginning, no one on the inland waterway ships has asked for a penny of tips. This is one thing.

Heavy taxes and miscellaneous fees are everywhere. Although the central government has clearly ordered their cancellation, there is still a school tax. In the past, there were no less than fifty or sixty kinds of taxes and fees for inland waterway ships, such as lump-sum tax, ticket tax, head tax, security tax, education tax, business association tax, and landing tax. We have completely abolished them. Except for the boat ticket, no extra money can be collected from passengers. This is the second thing.

Three customs offices have been established within Hubei Province. Therefore, goods from Shashi and Yichang to Hankou must pay a transit tax. Within a country, it is strange to call the movement from one place to another an export. It is unheard of in the world. Now, within a province, moving from one place to another to a third place is also called export and requires taxation, which is even more incomprehensible. As a result, local goods are piled up in the interior and cannot be sold, which is a major violation of the purpose of revitalizing rural areas. However, we cannot violate the central government's regulations. Moreover, the customs system involves internal and external debt credit. Therefore, under the premise of protecting local products and not changing the customs methods, ships on the upper reaches of the river do not directly go to Shashi and Yichang, but only to Ouchi. Transfer personnel are stationed in Ouchi, and offices are set up in Shashi. Goods from Han, Sha, and Yi are all transferred by boat in Ouchi, without delaying the date or increasing the transfer costs for passengers and merchants. In this way, the payment of transit tax is avoided, and the benefits are still obtained by the passengers and merchants. Although the customs detained the ship and negotiated several times, there is no problem now. This is the third thing.

Military police inspections along the way delay time and cause disputes. The inland navigation regulations of this office stipulate that inspections should be carried out on the wharf and on the shore. Except for the specified wharves, ships are absolutely not allowed to stop for loading or unloading or to load passengers and goods in the middle of the voyage, so as to avoid smuggling. This method has been discussed several times with the Tobacco Prohibition Supervision Office, the Salt Affairs Audit Office, and other local military police, and an understanding has been reached. We are cooperating in handling the matter. Therefore, ship inspections are no longer seen. I remember that the Hunan Provincial Rice Tax Bureau in Chenglingji ordered the ships of this office to stop for inspection and collect a tax of one yuan per dan of rice. This office believes that inland navigation does not operate in Hunan Province and has no obligation to accept inspection and pay taxes. The bureau's sentries fired several times with live ammunition, which was very dangerous. Later, after the provincial government sent a telegram to Hunan, the matter was brought under control. This is the fourth thing.

According to the regulations set by the Ministry, military police traveling on ships should purchase half-price tickets. This office has provided special convenience during the period of bandit suppression in this province. Those who have complete uniforms and symbols and carry passports and road passes are allowed to purchase free tickets. In addition, all others must purchase tickets and there is no half-price ticket policy. However, there are often non-active-duty military police, as well as recruits and yamen runners and police, who do not understand the rules and cause trouble. Fortunately, the senior officers of each team maintained traffic and strictly cracked down on and stopped them at any time. It is really overwhelming and troublesome. This is the fifth thing.

Small boats in the province were originally managed by the Construction Department. This sovereignty was recovered from the Customs in the fifteenth year of the Republic. In the twentieth year of the Republic, the Hankou Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications was established, and small boat inspection and measurement fees were re-collected. The Water Affairs Department stopped collecting inspection fees in 1922. Now, during the period of management, this office has no reason to collect them again. According to the principle of separation of powers between the central and local governments, provincial affairs belong to the local government. This point has already been understood by all parties, and the sixth difficulty has been overcome.

Travel dangers are common. Deception of passengers has now disappeared on ships. Only one robbery by bandits occurred last year on the Shenan ship on the Tianmen route. Thanks to the local military police and security teams, one bandit and one suspect were captured and are now being tried by military law. This deters the courage of thieves. This office has also concentrated the road navigation troops, strengthened training, purchased new-style guns, and deployed them in sections. We safely passed through last winter and solved the seventh difficulty.

The navigation routes in this province have rapid currents in summer and are shallow in winter. The Cangzibu and Tianmen routes are suspended in November. Although the Changjiangbu is separated by the X溝 shoal, a ship is left in X溝 this year to connect the routes, which can be said to be uninterrupted. The Shayang route was suspended in October in previous years. This year, pilots were hired to explore the waterway in sections and set up water markers, costing more than one thousand yuan, which allowed the route to be maintained every day throughout the year. The other routes were never interrupted, and they did not stop operating during the Lunar New Year. Although it is easy to do, no one has done it before. This is the eighth thing.

The dispatch of military transport ships accounts for one-fourth. Large ships are selected, and at the same time, all routes must be maintained. In addition, it is necessary to cope with the crowded passengers and goods at the end of the lunar year. I had to use tugboats to replace them and barely got through it. This is the ninth difficulty.

Most of the ships under management are rotten and broken. We set up a machine shop to repair them ourselves. The machine shop has no start-up funds and uses old machines. With only three thousand yuan of working capital, we barely managed to get through it. This is the tenth difficulty.

Other trivial difficulties are encountered every day and every moment, and there is no need to go into details. In short, we have solved them with all our heart, all our strength, and all our spirit.

What is our goal in spending our energy to do this? Is it to earn some bonuses for the government? No, we have been trying it out for a year to test a policy, which is the management method of public utilities. Commercial operations have failed, and government operations are also unstable. Government supervision and commercial operations have even more perfunctory abuses. We supervised the Jingcheng Electric Light Company in the past and did not get good results. Now we are proposing "commercial supervision and public operation." The Supervisory Committee of Inland Navigation is actually commercial supervision, with representatives from the Chamber of Commerce and the Bankers' Association, and accountants to check the accounts. Unfortunately, the shipping merchants have not used cooperation and goodwill to supervise. On the public operation side, the government has done its best, fulfilled its promise, and distributed bonuses. If it were not for public operation, given the current economic downturn, I don't know how much the shipping industry would have declined, and the above-mentioned ten difficulties could not have been solved at all. Now that we have been trying it out for a year, our method has proven to be sound. "Commercial supervision and public operation" can be applied to all public utilities. This policy adopts the Anglo-American advocacy of protecting capital and applies the Russian-German method of control and management, combining the strengths of others to suit China's national conditions. However, its organization must be more strict and definite and not be affected by politics. Only then can the foundation of the business be as solid as a rock. Detailed designs cannot be reported here. We must wait for the provincial government to decide whether inland navigation will be like this in the future. We do not know yet. We have repeatedly reduced the prices of tickets and goods for inland navigation, also to test a policy. According to economics, rising prices lead to industrial development, and rising living standards improve the people's level. However, in China, the ratio of prices to living expenses is too different compared to foreign countries. American coal miners can earn an average of three yuan a day and buy a loaf of bread for only five cents. Therefore, they can buy sixty loaves of bread a day. Chinese workers only earn three cents a day, and if a loaf of bread also costs five cents, they can only buy six loaves of bread a day. If calculated in American gold dollars, a loaf of bread costs five gold dollars, which is equivalent to one point five Chinese yuan. Then Chinese workers can only buy two loaves of bread a day. American coal costs three yuan per ton, while Chinese coal costs ten yuan per ton. An American car costs five hundred yuan, but it costs three thousand yuan in China. An American movie costs five cents, while a Chinese movie costs five cents, or at least two cents. And the salary of Chinese people, it is very good to earn thirty yuan. A very small position in England can also earn one hundred yuan a month. Not counting the exchange rate between the US dollar and the national currency, if the ratio of living expenses to salary for Americans is assumed to be one, then it is ten times for Chinese people. This is really living with the consumption of the 20th century with the income of the 18th century. How can it not be difficult to be exhausted? It is unreasonable to increase the income of Chinese people to improve living standards. Our country has no money at all, and prices continue to rise due to layers of interaction, making it difficult to reach the European and American standards. We turn around and want to reduce prices to suit the amount of income. Based on the ratio of living income, Chinese coal should be sold for one yuan per ton. In fact, Shanxi coal is very cheap, at most two yuan per ton. However, due to high shipping costs and other reasons, it sells for ten yuan in Hankou. We can do our best to reduce prices in terms of shipping costs. Domestic shipping costs are really too expensive. For example, the shipping cost of a ton of tung oil from Yichang to Hankou is twelve yuan, while the shipping cost from Hankou to Shanghai is only six yuan. The distance is doubled, but the shipping cost is halved. The shipping cost from Shanghai to the United States is only three US dollars. The distance is increased tenfold, but the cost is reduced tenfold. This situation can be studied. We want to help lower prices without lowering the benefits of living, support the circulation of rural local products, and resist the dumping of tens of thousands of yuan of foreign goods. This policy of suppressing prices is not the Anglo-American policy of currency inflation, but seeks self-sufficiency in products, adopts the Indian policy of non-cooperation and self-sufficiency, and the Japanese policy of revitalizing industry and commerce and low-price manufacturing, and the policy of cheap goods and peace under heaven in our country's dynasties. It is determined that this can revive the Chinese economy. Now shipping costs are a very small part, and most of it is still in the production and sales agencies. Although we cannot prove the effectiveness of this policy with numbers today, the activities of various industries and businesses in the province over the past year have indeed made us know that this road is correct. The relationship between suppressing prices and all aspects is too complicated. Military affairs, politics, transportation, finance, currency system, tax rules, industry, and commerce are all locked together. I am not an economist, and I don't know what theories to cite, but I can cite a very obvious fact as a conclusion. The price of coal in Xi'an used to be thirty yuan per ton, but now that the Longhai Railway is open to traffic, it has been reduced to eight yuan per ton. As a result, two new yarn factories have been established. Yarn factories can never use coal at thirty yuan per ton. This is the key to our economic revival."

Pessimistic Outlook for Commerce in Guangdong Province

Taishan County Markets Do Not Allow Credit Sales

Both Imports and Exports Decreased Last Year

Guangzhou Communication: Since the beginning of spring, commerce in Guangdong Province has remained as sluggish as ever. The Economic Planning Association, affiliated with the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce, has sent a letter to the City Chamber of Commerce to decide on relief policies in order to solve the recovery of commerce in the city in the future, so that planning can be carried out. The fundamental reason for the decline of the market is the weak purchasing power of the people. The reason for the weak purchasing power is that foreign trade has plummeted in recent years. At the same time, the amount of money remitted to the mainland by overseas Chinese has decreased. Taking Taishan County in Guangdong Province as an example, the county has the largest number of overseas Chinese and is known as a wealthy county. After the United States banned the export of gold, the county's working capital completely stopped. In Taishan last year, I don't know how many stores closed down. This spring, transactions in the area have changed to a cash system, and credit sales are not allowed. In the past month, credit sales have been banned. The desolation of the market can be seen. It is heard that the regulations prohibiting credit sales in the market were issued and implemented yesterday by the Yong'an Market and Chonglou Market Chambers of Commerce in the county. The regulations stipulate: (1) All stores in this market should use cash transactions as the standard for retail sales, and should not extend credit out of sentiment to maintain capital; (2) All retail sales and wholesale sales should be based on cash transactions in principle, but for transactions between stores in the market, such as taking goods in and out with ledgers, they should be settled once a month to facilitate circulation; (3) For any store that does not comply with the regulations, once found, it will be severely punished; (4) These regulations will be implemented from the eighth day of the first month of the lunar year of the Republic of China. According to the usual practice in the Guangdong market, reliance is placed on credit and borrowing. Often, with 10,000 yuan in cash, merchants operate businesses worth 100,000 yuan. Now that the new regulations have been issued, funds cannot be used actively. It may be possible to maintain the status quo, but it is not necessarily possible to develop.

As for the province's foreign trade, both imports and exports decreased last year, and the trade deficit reached more than 78 million yuan. According to the statistics bureau's investigation, from the 19th to the 23rd year of the Republic of China, the total value of the comparison between the import of foreign goods and the export of local goods in Guangdong Province is as follows: (1) In the 19th year of the Republic of China, the import of foreign goods was 25,075,377 yuan, and the export of local goods was 16,465,3676 yuan. The trade deficit that year was 86,096,701 yuan; (2) In the 20th year, the import of foreign goods was 25,526,284 yuan, and the export of local goods was 15,203,4721 yuan, with a trade deficit of 10,322,7563 yuan; (3) In the 21st year, the import of foreign goods was 31,425,8054 yuan, and the export of local goods was 93,538,205 yuan, with a trade deficit of 22,172,0849 yuan; (4) In the 22nd year, the import of foreign goods was 26,922,000 yuan, and the export of local goods was 94,400,354 yuan, with a trade deficit of 17,476,1646 yuan; (5) In the 23rd year, the import of foreign goods was 15,655,3123 yuan, and the export of local goods was 78,252,674 yuan, with a trade deficit of 78,300,449 yuan. All of the above five years show a trade deficit, and the total amount of the trade deficit for the five years reached 664,100,7208 yuan. Judging from the above figures, the import of foreign goods was the highest in the 21st year, and the export of local goods was also the lowest. Last year (the 23rd year) the trade deficit was the smallest, and on the surface it seems optimistic, but in reality, it is a reflection of the sharp decline in the purchasing power of the people of Guangdong and the exhaustion of the social economy.

Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Bureau Surveys the Nanping Section

Earthwork of the Yunan Section Has Been Completed

Yushan Communication: The Nanchang-Pingxiang section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is now under planning. The bureau has organized a Nanping Road survey team and appointed Lan Tian as the surveying director and Li Zhaode as the investigation director. They set off to conduct a field survey along the road. The provincial government has ordered the governments and garrisons of Nanchang, Xinjian, Fengcheng, Qingjiang, Xinyu, Fenyi, Yichun, Shanggao, Wan'an, Wanzai, and Pingxiang counties to provide effective protection and cooperate with the team in surveying and investigating. The Liangjiadu Bridge on the section was originally agreed upon by the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Bureau and the Provincial Highway Bureau to build a joint railway and highway bridge in Liangjiadu. The required funds have recently been decided by the Provincial Affairs Conference to be allocated from the Highway Bureau's construction fee. Materials have been ordered from the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Bureau and construction is underway day and night. As for the section from Yu to Nanchang, after the General Bureau set a deadline for completion and opening to traffic on the Double Tenth Festival, the various projects on the section are progressing actively. The earthwork of the entire section has been completed, and it is expected that this section of the project can be completed in October of this year. (February 27)

Songjiang

Grand Opening of the New Songjiang Society

Shen Lianbi and others, aware that Songjiang's municipal construction is progressing day by day, but there is still no proper organization to promote local welfare, jointly with outstanding members of the county, initiated the New Songjiang Society in the spring of the 21st year. For a time, they followed suit and expanded more than 30 mu of land next to the Songwei Motor Road to build a meeting place, forming more than ten buildings of houses and flat houses, with a large square in the middle, which is quite like a garden. Members are divided into four types: permanent, ordinary, sponsor, and student, and now there are more than 400 people, with the aim of connecting friendship, exchanging knowledge, promoting physical education, and improving society. After two years of planning, the opening ceremony was held today (3rd) at 9:00 am. Silver shields and couplets donated by all sectors were dazzling. Such as the congratulations from Chairman Lin, Dean Wang, Liu Yazi, Tang Shengzhi, Yao Yuanchu, Zhao Zukang, etc., and those who came to participate in person were members of the Central Committee Cai Yuan and were appreciated by all sectors.

Wuxi

Dredging of Six Major Rivers Begins

The provincial office for dredging the Zhenzheng section of the canal has designated to recruit 1,800 laborers from Wumu to Shitangwan in Luoshe, Wuxi, to dredge six major rivers. Yesterday, the County Construction Bureau specially sent the head of the technical section Huang Dechun, technicians Xu Chuzhen and Xu Chuanlie to the 10th, 2nd and 4th districts to convene river dredging meetings and guide the construction of dams and allocation of work. The Nanma Ligang and Changguangxi rivers in the 10th and 3rd districts have been dammed and construction has begun. The remaining Li尖 River in the 2nd district, the Lv River in the 4th district, the Beixingtang River, which will be dredged in the 6th and 7th districts, and the Xizhang section of the Xiantang River in the 5th district, are all actively underway and can be started within days. Wang Shixi, an engineer from the Construction Department, was ordered to inspect the river dredging projects in the 17 counties of Jiangnan and came to Wuxi the day before yesterday to guide everything.

A Husband Kills His Wife in an Argument

Zhou Deming, 22 years old, from Yancheng, a resident of the Caopeng Lane in Lixiang near the Caishen Lane outside the west gate of Wuxi, works as a cart puller. His wife, Tao, 21 years old, works as a female worker in the silkworm cocoon copying room of the Jinji Silk Factory in the west gate. They have a daughter who is still young. The couple usually had arguments from time to time. Yesterday (2nd) at about 3:00 am, they suddenly had another argument over a trivial matter. Zhou Deming became angry and took a piece of western pine wood pillow and hit Tao's head hard, causing a hole in her forehead, blood flowed straight, and she fell on the bed. Before long, she died. Chen Huiyou, the head of the fourth Bao Nianerjia in that area, reported to the fourth branch of the Public Security Bureau, and the murderer Zhou Deming was arrested and taken to the bureau for custody. Chen Zizhao, the head of the 227th Tu, reported to the local branch court and requested an autopsy. At 2:00 pm, the coroner, accompanied by Wang Jian, went to perform the autopsy and confirmed that she had died from injuries sustained before death. After the autopsy, the coroner ordered the corpse to be prepared for burial. The murderer, Zhou Deming, will be transferred to the General Bureau today and then to the Prosecutor's Office for investigation and handling.

Changshu

Donation for Reconstruction of Canghai Temple

Canghai Temple, one of the four famous Zen temples on the summit of Mount Yu, held a grand gathering on the Shangsi Festival last year. That night, a fire broke out unexpectedly. The ancient temple, deep in the mountains, had no way to call for help, resulting in the destruction of this wonderful ancient temple, turning it to ashes. Since then, the foot of Mount Yu has lost a scenic spot, which is a great regret to the local people. It is now known that the abbot of the temple has been running around and appealing to the local gentry, planning to raise funds for reconstruction. This matter concerns the scenic spots of the county and has received assistance from various parties. Plans are underway to raise funds for reconstruction. However, due to the labor and time required on the summit of the mountain, the funds needed will certainly exceed ordinary construction. The estimated funds needed are fifty to sixty thousand dollars. Efforts are currently being made to solicit donations from all parties and overseas Chinese in order to restore the original beauty of Mount Yu.

Zhenjiang

Hengyu Ferry Robbery Case Solved

The Hengyu ferry of the Yangzi Company's Zhenqing line was robbed by bandits between the Dagang Bridge to the south and the large and small culverts in Baoying County. After receiving the report, the provincial government, considering the Grand Canal as an important waterway for navigation in northern Jiangsu, and that the bandits dared to rob ships, was extremely angry. It immediately telegraphed the Baoying County magistrate and the head of the 4th District of the Provincial Water Police to strictly investigate and arrest the bandits within a limited time. It is now heard that the case has been solved by the 2nd Squadron of the 19th Team of the 4th District of the Water Police in Gejia Village, Baoying, with the arrest of bandit Zhu Shouxi. A camel hair coat and a wolf skin rug were found in the bandit's home. Subsequently, Zhao Hengchun was intercepted in Huai'an County, along with the stolen goods. Recently, Magistrate Zhou of Baoying County led a team to round up fourteen people, including Dong Yuzhen, in Huai'an, and a portion of the stolen goods have been escorted to the Baoying County Government for interrogation according to law, and for the stolen goods to be claimed.

Seven Bandits Executed by the County Government

A special agent of the Zhenjiang County Government, together with the 1st Branch of the Public Security Bureau, previously arrested Feng Pengzhang, a bandit involved in the kidnapping of Hua Yin of Hua Village in the 4th District of the county. In addition, the captain of the 2nd Security Brigade successively arrested Wang Shilan and Zhu Yaodong, who were kidnapped in Lingtang Township of the 3rd District, and Feng Dayuan, Pan Hegui, Zhang Litian, Yu Liusan, and Zhang Rusheng, bandits involved in the robbery and kidnapping cases in the houses of Cao Rufu and Wang Qingzhen of Qingfeng Township in the 2nd District. Dai Laoda, a bandit, was also arrested by the Shuyang County Government upon request and brought to the county. After interrogation, all confessed to the crimes without denial. The provincial government approved the execution. On the morning of the 2nd, at 7:00 a.m., the bandits were taken to the execution ground outside the North Gate and executed by firing squad.

Jiangsu Coastal Pirates to be Completely Eliminated

Coastal pirates were discovered in the coastal areas of Jiangsu Province at the end of last year, and their activities were quite rampant. The provincial government ordered the complete mobilization of the 3rd District of the Provincial Water Police to suppress them within two months. It also dispatched the Ce Dian, Jing Hai, and Jing Dong patrol ships to patrol the Xiaosha area for rear defense. After departing on the mission, they passed through Rugao Yang and advanced north on January 3 of this year. Based on reports that a number of pirate ships were in the Huanghejian and Taozikou areas, they sailed through Xinyang Port and advanced north for encirclement and suppression. They also telegraphed Funing County to send teams to prevent blockades. On January 10 and 11, they came into contact with the pirates in the waters near Taozikou and Chaohekou, capturing four pirate ships, six guns, capturing thirty-three pirates, killing four pirates, and seventy or eighty people throwing their guns into the sea. The remaining pirates escaped by boat into Taozikou. After investigation, Taozikou is under the jurisdiction of Funing County, with barren suburbs on three sides, mixed with reeds, and a coastline of silt and sand beaches. Due to the terrain, it was not possible to immediately pursue them deeply. The remaining pirates took advantage of the north wind and the tide to escape south by boat. The provincial government, upon receiving the report, ordered all coastal counties to block coastal ports to prevent the pirates from landing and escaping, or from seeking supplies. At the same time, it strictly ordered the water police to track and intercept them. On February 10, a fierce battle with the pirates took place in the waters of Dongsha, Dongtai, capturing two pirate ships, capturing more than ten pirates, killing dozens of pirates, seizing four guns, one earthen cannon, and rescuing three hostages. Three water police officers were injured. The remaining pirates broke through the encirclement. On February 13 and 14, another encirclement and suppression was carried out in the waters north of Doulong Port, destroying one pirate ship belonging to the pirate leader Yu Sanduanzi, seizing one Yantai cannon, eight guns, killing more than ten people including the pirate leader Yu Sanduanzi, and rescuing one hostage and two boatmen. A wallet, business cards, and private seals were found on Yu's body. Two water police patrol leaders and one water patrol officer were injured. One boatman was killed. The remaining twenty or so pirates have collapsed and are no longer a force. The anti-piracy troops are still searching and suppressing them, and it is expected that they will be completely eliminated soon.

It is truly tragic.

Xiaoshan

Unemployed Merchant Commits Suicide by Castration

Wang Shanshe, a merchant from Dongwang, a village west of Xiaoshan, used to work as an accountant in a guiyuan shop in Shanghai. Last year, affected by the situation, he was laid off and returned home to sit idle. Almost a year passed, and his family was large, making it difficult to make a living. At the beginning of last month, he suddenly became mentally disturbed. On the night of the 28th, he took advantage of his family's inattention and used scissors to cut off his genitals. He immediately shouted in pain, and blood flowed all over the bed, leading to his death. His family tried to save him, but he was already breathless and dead.

Local News

Silver and Money Industries Resume Accepting Real Estate Mortgages

Land Prices Showing Signs of Recovery, Financial Situation Gradually Stabilizing

Reducing Credit Lending, Maximizing Acceptance of Goods as Collateral

Xinsheng News Agency reports that after the Local Association, the City Chamber of Commerce, and other groups convened to discuss rescuing the market, the silver and money industries have resumed accepting real estate mortgages, and the financial situation is gradually stabilizing. The details are as follows:

Real Estate Mortgages Resume Being Accepted

In the past, it was customary for the silver and money industries to accept real estate mortgages as the only sound business, because real estate is immobile and its value is stable. Banks at home and abroad were happy to accept it as collateral. Since last year, due to the emergency in the money market and the sharp drop in real estate prices, the silver and money industries unanimously rejected real estate mortgages. If they were accepted, restrictions were very strict, resulting in sluggish real estate. Since the Local Association and other groups convened to discuss rescue measures, the silver and money industries have resumed accepting real estate mortgages, depending on their own strength. Therefore, today's real estate is slightly more active than before, and its prices are also showing signs of recovery.

Maximum Acceptance of Goods as Collateral

After the final accounting of the Republic of China in 1934, the foreign exchange rate announced daily in the money industry market was always at eight or nine points, and every year, after the final accounting, when the money industry began to send folds and lend money, it was always at the white exchange rate. Therefore, although the Shanghai money market is looser than last year, it has not fully recovered. The silver and money industries are very cautious about credit lending and are maximizing the acceptance of goods as collateral in order to achieve the goal of recovery. Therefore, Shanghai's financial industry is gradually stabilizing and is expected to fully recover after a considerable period of time.

The Shenxin No. 7 Factory Incident Is Expected to Be Resolved Within the Week

HSBC Is Considering the Solutions Proposed by Our Side

Rong Zongjing Talks About the Past Dangerous Period of Shenxin

Central News Agency reports that after the HSBC Bank in Shanghai auctioned off the No. 7 Factory of the Shenxin Textile Company without authorization, people from all walks of life were filled with righteous indignation, and the government also paid close attention. The Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry are actively planning rescue measures. At present, as a result of negotiations with the Shanghai Municipal Government to the HSBC Bank, HSBC has generally agreed to consider paying 250,000 yuan of the overdue interest in advance, and the remaining debt will be repaid in full in four months in order to redeem the No. 7 Factory. However, the specific plan will still be finalized after Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi arrives in Shanghai. Last night, a reporter from the Central News Agency made a special trip to the residence of Rong Zongjing, General Manager of the Shenxin Company, to interview Rong and ask about his latest thoughts on the No. 7 Factory incident. Rong immediately denied with a very indignant attitude that the "If the government can redeem the No. 7 Factory, the factory is willing to be state-owned, and the banking consortium must also be assumed by the government" in a certain evening newspaper yesterday, saying that it was completely inaccurate. He continued, "This time, I am deeply grateful for the assistance of the government and society. At present, HSBC's attitude has gradually softened, and it has agreed to consider redeeming it in installments, which may come to an end in the middle of this week. As for the entire Shenxin Textile Company problem, since last year, due to the export of silver and the extremely tight money market, banks and money houses were unable to take care of themselves, causing Shenxin to fall into extreme difficulty. At present, the financial situation has loosened, and we are contacting banks and money houses separately for mortgage loans. If it can be successful in a short time, we will proceed to redeem it. Since the reform of Shenxin last year, the situation has become more stable day by day. The No. 7 Factory is still working as usual, and has not stopped working on Sundays. Recently, due to the large amount of inventory, the market is small, and the market is quite popular. The dangerous period has now passed."

The Social Affairs Bureau Bans Recruitment for Overseas Labor

The Social Affairs Bureau issued a notice yesterday to ban the recruitment of labor for overseas jobs, stating that it has recently been reported by citizens that some people have privately established a recruitment agency in the Guandi Temple in the West Gate of the city, inducing poor workers to go abroad to work in mines with high interest, resulting in the enlistment of a general uneducated worker. They said they would first take a ship to Xiamen, transfer to go abroad. The trip would take 18 days and nights. After landing, they would transfer to the train to the iron mine. This kind of act, which is close to selling piglets, has been seen many times in the past, and the outflow of Chinese workers who blindly go abroad is very harmful. Please investigate. According to the dispatched staff investigation report, the monks of the temple admitted that this was the case, and more than 30 workers from Shandong had been recruited to follow them. However, the truth of the contents is unknown, and the person in charge of recruitment has left the temple and gone elsewhere. The private recruitment of labor for overseas jobs has countless evils, and the temple did not report to the competent authority for approval when it allowed criminals to privately set up recruitment agencies during the winter defense period. In light of the previous situation, it is difficult to guarantee that the criminals have not secretly moved their residences or plotting something, and this matter must be investigated and prohibited. In addition to notifying the citizens, everyone should be aware of it, and do not fall into the tricks of criminals, and also send a letter to the Public Security Bureau for a thorough investigation, and instruct all subordinates to investigate and prohibit it.

China Aviation Company Actively Assembling Large Ford Aircraft

Expected to Be Assembled in Mid-Month

China Aviation Company, in order to open the Shanghai-Yunnan route, purchased a large Ford aircraft from the United States at a price of 150,000 yuan, because the route is full of mountains and ridges. The aircraft arrived in Shanghai from the United States on the 1st of this month, and was immediately unloaded at the Longhua Airport. American engineers are supervising the craftsmen to assemble it. It is expected to be assembled in mid-month. At that time, a short-distance test flight will be conducted in Shanghai. If the results are good, the Shanghai-Yunnan route will be tested on a scheduled basis. According to the company, the specialty of the large Ford aircraft is that it is structurally strong and durable. City Chamber of Commerce Cables the Legislative Yuan Again, Requesting Prompt Enactment of the Commercial Registration Law

Adopting a Proportional Share System

To Revive Declining Commerce

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce yesterday cabled the Legislative Yuan in Nanjing, stating: "To the Honorable Legislative Yuan, Nanjing: The Commercial Registration Law, stipulating the issue of joint and several liability, is in line with the effectiveness of regulating the current Article 681 of the Civil Code. This was proposed by the Honorable Yuan's legislators and has received the sympathy and support of various local chambers of commerce. Regarding the reasons for advocating joint and several liability, our Chamber submitted documents to the Honorable Yuan on March 10, 1933, June 26 of the same year, and November 6 of the previous year, repeatedly and exhaustively detailing the arguments. We have recently heard that the preliminary review of this registration law has been completed. However, regarding the issue of partnership liability, there are those who advocate the adoption of a joint liability system, which has caused hesitation and indecision, leaving the matter unresolved. Upon investigation, the only difference between joint liability and joint and several liability is that the creditor has no right of choice. In terms of the actual responsibility borne by the debtor, it is still the same as joint and several liability. Our Chamber, in its presentation on November 6 of the previous year, already provided a detailed analysis of the inconveniences of this system. In the past, various chambers of commerce have repeatedly voiced their disapproval of the former Supreme Court's precedents on this matter, stating that they are not in line with national conditions. There are documents that can be examined. Some argue that the current proposed system is designed with the interests of creditors in mind, as if the merchants represented by the chamber of commerce are entirely in the position of debtors. This is far from the truth and needs no further explanation. Currently, the commercial market is in a dangerous situation, with businesses closing down one after another. Those who can barely sustain themselves are also afraid of future burdens and are generally thinking of shrinking their operations. Those with meager assets are also afraid of the heavy responsibility and dare not engage in commerce. If this continues, it is feared that there will only be successive contractions and no new developments. Whether a legislative policy is appropriate or not can always influence the social economy. At this critical juncture of the survival or demise of commerce, our Chamber has a deep understanding and dares to disregard the risk of offense and reiterate our previous request. We humbly request that your esteemed department adopt the original draft of Article 9 of the drafting members of the Commercial Registration Law, submit the law to the Yuan for discussion as soon as possible, and pass it for implementation to revive declining commerce and comfort the anxious commercial sentiment. This would be a public convenience. The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce kowtows. Winter."

The Municipal Public Security Bureau to Move to New Location Within the Month

Renovation Work at the New Site Progressing Actively

Personnel to be Deployed After Completion Within Days

The Xin Xin News Agency reports: The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, due to the dilapidated state of its original location in the old Daotai Yamen in the Nanshi district, which was unsuitable for office use, purchased a property from the Shanghai County Government on Penglai Road, formerly the Shanghai County Government office, consisting of approximately 60-70 buildings. Sheng Yunji Construction Company was contracted to renovate the property and build new facilities, including a car park, a repair shop, a detective team office, and a detention center. The original deadline for completion and handover was the end of last year. However, due to issues with the construction permit and the relocation of residents, the deadline could not be met as scheduled. As the bureau urgently needed to move in, it repeatedly set deadlines. It has now been over five months. The contracting company has been working overtime in recent days to accelerate the construction, and most of the work, including the interior decoration and painting, has been completed. The new facilities are expected to be completed within days.

Buildings Divided into Three Sections

The new location of the bureau is divided as follows: the front section will house the reception room, mail room, military band room, foreign guest reception room, and male and female detention rooms. The second section will house the director's office, various department offices, and archives. The rear section will house the detective team and detention center. The east side building will house the accounting office, general affairs office, and the lost and kidnapped women and children reception room. The west side building will house the medical officer's office, the overseas passport office, and the foreign registration office. Three buildings behind the east side building will serve as the case reception room and preliminary hearing court. Behind the four side buildings are several newly built car parks and repair shops.

Move-in Within the Month

According to the person in charge of the Sheng Yunji Construction Company yesterday, due to the expiration of the deadline, they have been working overtime to accelerate the construction, which has been quite hectic. They originally planned to hand over the property yesterday, but some minor details are still incomplete, such as the rewiring of several lights and the construction of pedestrian walkways. Therefore, it will be delayed for a few more days. Everything can be completed at once. However, according to the planned schedule, the property must be handed over within days. Once the various interior works are completed and cleaned, the Public Security Bureau plans to come and arrange everything, and it is expected to officially move in and begin operations around the middle of this month.

Inscription on the Monument to the Loyal Martyrs of Jiangwan

Expected to be Completed Around the End of the Month

During the January 28 Incident, countless soldiers and civilians died. After the ceasefire, people in Jiangwan collected over 1,300 bodies and built a cemetery for the loyal martyrs on the site. This project began long ago and is expected to be completed around the end of this month. A memorial archway is being built in front of the cemetery entrance, and the inscription for the monument has been written. The Municipal Government has approved the Public Works Bureau's request to build a monument to the loyal martyrs from the Moon Stone Bridge in Jiangwan to the cemetery. The original text of the inscription is recorded below: "Inscription on the Monument to the Loyal Martyrs of Jiangwan January 28." "On the night of January 28, 1932, the Japanese army invaded our Zhabei and attacked Wusong. Unable to succeed with all their might, they concentrated their forces on Jiangwan. On February 20, they ordered a general offensive. Our Jiangwan territory, with its prosperous towns and densely populated villages, was reduced to scorched earth in less than ten days. Alas, how cruel! In mid-March, the war had just ended. Cai Weizhang and Lu Chengyu, directors of the Chongshan Hall, and others, could not bear to see the anti-Japanese soldiers and fallen compatriots lying dead in the fields. Therefore, they organized a burial team, raised funds, selected personnel, and developed a plan, working diligently day and night. Despite the restrictions imposed by the enemy army, they did not slacken in their efforts to prevent exposure. In the winter of that year, they opened up over nine acres of public land in Changgouwan, north of the town, and gathered the bodies buried in the suburbs and buried them in a single mound in the new Western style to comfort the loyal souls. Two years later, they again raised funds to build a memorial archway, a tomb house, open up thoroughfares, and plant flowers and trees, completing the entire project. The sacrifices of the people in the January 28 Incident were enormous, and the survival of the nation depended on it. Without a little magnificence to inspire the public's aspirations and to seek revenge, the responsibility falls on those who come after. How can we merely see this as the benevolent burying of bones? In this incident, 1,300 bodies were buried, not including those buried in Guangzhao Mountain Villa. Over 15,000 yuan was spent. Yan Enpu, a fellow villager, independently donated 500 silver dollars for the memorial monument. Wang Weiguan from Ningbo donated over 10,000 silver dollars for burial expenses. Their enthusiasm for public welfare and their leadership in advocating for this are commendable. The other individuals who contributed their efforts and donations will be remembered separately. They are not listed here. Written respectfully by Shen Mingshi, a fellow villager, on New Year's Day, 1935."

Intestine Industry Guild Discusses Steps to Compel Members to Join

The Intestine Industry Guild of this city, regarding the case of compelling members of the same industry to join, recently received a public letter from the Judicial Yuan, Yuan Zi No. 1161, stating that the case has been resolved by the Unified Interpretation of Laws Conference. The original text of Article 7 of the Industry and Commerce Guild Law, the words "may," have been revised to "shall." Therefore, companies and firms in the same industry should be forced to join the guild. Therefore, the guild is scheduled to convene a temporary meeting at 4:00 PM today to discuss the steps to compel members of the same industry to join. They will also jointly request the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward a request to the authorities to announce and implement the compulsory measures so that the rights and interests of the same industry can be popularized as soon as possible.

Dai Chaofu Dies Unexpectedly

At around 9:00 AM yesterday, a No. 14 streetcar of the China Merchants, traveling south from north, was passing the Yongsheng Wharf in the Nanshi district when a porter, Dai Chaofu (25 years old, from Jiangbei, living in a thatched shed west of Sanguantang in Pudong) and another porter carried a long, large piece of timber out of the Yifeng Lumber Company, intending to cross the road. Dai Chaofu walked a bit slower, causing the streetcar to arrive, and he was unable to avoid it. He was knocked to the ground, and the timber he was carrying fell on his head. Instantly, his skull was shattered, his brain matter burst out, and he lost consciousness. Zhao Gengyang, the watchman of the 16th Gang in that area, heard the news and rushed to the scene. He immediately transported the injured Dai Chaofu to the Shanghai Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his injuries, the treatment was ineffective, and he soon died. The streetcar driver, Fu Baoyin, was taken to the Dongjiadu Police Station under the jurisdiction of Yi, the station chief, for questioning. Because the case involved a human life, he was ordered to prepare a document to be submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation. At the same time, the local Jia was dispatched to report to the Shanghai District Court to send someone to conduct an autopsy.

Flower Tailor, Major Suspect in Homicide Case, Awaits Sentencing

Flower Tailor, a native of Anhui, 27 years old, also known as Yan Zhi, residing at No. 12 Puai Fang, Zhoujia Pai Road, on the fourth day of the first lunar month, quarreled with his neighbor, Qin Maobiao, 29 years old, also from Anhui, over a debt of three yuan owed by Yuan. Qin slapped him in the face and had his friend, Cao Laowu, beat him. Flower, outnumbered, took the opportunity to escape and stayed with a friend in Ziteng Gang, Minhang. At around 9:00 PM on the 14th of last month, Flower came to Shanghai for business. He was spotted by Qin near Haizhou Road, Ningwu Road. Qin asked him to go to the Sanyuan Fang teahouse on Yangshupu Road to talk, but he refused, and another brawl broke out. Yang Guifu, a local, and Cao Fushou, from Anhui, tried to mediate, but neither side would give in, saying that they had to kill one of them. Yang, fearing that a major incident would cause trouble for them, said, "If you act like this, I will report you to the police," and ran away. Flower and Qin saw this and fled north. As a result, they continued to fight fiercely half a mile away, falling into a river. Qin was seriously injured and died on the beach. Flower escaped and returned to Minhang. After the case was reported, Zhang Yunjian, a Chinese detective from the Yangshupu Police Station, discovered his hiding place and arrested him, sending him to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, Judge Wu Zehan of the Third Criminal Court interrogated the defendant. He confessed that he did not intentionally want to kill him at the time. It was the deceased who provoked him, causing this unfortunate incident. He asked for leniency. Judge Wu appointed lawyer Jiang Baoli to defend the defendant and ordered him to be remanded in custody, setting a date for sentencing.

Huaying Pharmacy Creditors' Meeting Resolved to Resume Business Yesterday

Twelve Representatives Elected on the Spot

Verify Accounts and Discuss Solutions

Huaying Pharmacy on Nanjing Road, due to financial difficulties, was resolved by the shareholders to suspend business in all branches from the 1st of this month and to entrust accountant Xie Lin to announce the liquidation. Mr. Xie notified all creditors to convene a meeting at the Daya Lou Restaurant on Fuzhou Road at 2:00 PM yesterday. Over 200 people attended, representing a total of 900,000 yuan in creditor rights. First, Mr. Xie reported the purpose of the meeting and a brief overview of the accounts. Then, 12 creditors verified the accounts and discussed solutions. The details are recorded below.

Report on Accounts

Mr. Xie reported the accounts, including 100,000 yuan in share capital under liabilities, 50,000 yuan in mortgage loans, over 31,000 yuan in deposit guarantees, over 161,000 yuan in unpaid goods, over 179,000 yuan owed to various banks and money shops, over 783,000 yuan in deposits. Assets included over 623,000 yuan in inventory, over 212,000 yuan in real estate, over 40,000 yuan in property, over 40,000 yuan in deposit guarantees, over 175,000 yuan in customer debts, over 83,000 yuan in temporary debts, over 49,000 yuan owed by branches, over 45,000 yuan in losses, totaling over 1.338 million yuan.

Shareholders' Resolution

Mr. Xie continued, "From the above asset and liability situation, it can be seen that there is too much inventory, and it is difficult to recover external debts, resulting in financial difficulties. The sluggish market is also an important reason. The company's shareholders held a meeting to discuss that, fearing the market downturn and that deposits would only go out and not come in, regardless of legal facts, there was only dissolution and liquidation to avoid increasing losses. Otherwise, lawsuits would pile up, fearing that the balance would be lost. Therefore, at the shareholders' meeting on February 28, it was resolved to dissolve and liquidate, and accountant Xie was selected as the liquidator to legally conclude the matter."

Deliberations on the Aftermath

"However, the pharmacy business is not the same as ordinary stores. It may not be easy to get a good price when selling goods. If the creditors have a proper solution, the shareholders and directors will all comply. Therefore, this accountant was entrusted to convey this intention, so we are holding a meeting today to discuss. In my opinion, the company's assets and liabilities are of such a large amount, the original share capital is only 100,000 yuan, and the losses are almost half. It is also a limited company, so the aftermath is very important to the creditors. The creditors should make their own decisions to save the situation."

Resolution to Resume Business

After discussions among the creditors on the spot, everyone said that the pharmacy has a long history. The suspension of business this time is due to the accumulation of inventory, and it is possible to resume business. It was resolved that the resumption of business should be carried out and that 12 representatives should be elected, one representative for every 100,000 yuan of creditor rights. Ding Mengxian, Shao Jingfu, Pu Lianming, Zhang Yiling, Ren Zhujun, Zhang Jingbang, Tian Yunda, Chen Tinghe, and others were elected on the spot. The above are deposit representatives. The goods representatives are Shenchang Foreign Firm and Yimoke Foreign Firm. As for the two representatives of the silver industry, they are outside the meeting and will be elected on their own. After the meeting, the representatives exchanged views and decided to first consult the account books at accountant Xie's office and then decide on a solution.
