Free Talk

On the Influence Received by Writers

— He Jin

Every writer, in the process of writing, will inevitably be influenced by others to some extent, intentionally or unintentionally; such examples can be readily cited: In the sentence structure of Alexander Fadeyev, one can see many contours of Tolstoy; and the early works of the new American writer William Faulkner are almost entirely filled with the crisp, strange style of Gertrude Stein; in addition, there is Paul Morand's influence on Japanese writer Yokomitsu Riichi and American writer J. Heigeshimer; L. Kassil, the Soviet newcomer famous for writing "Uibandpanua," was indeed somewhat influenced by Mayakovsky; and finally, looking at the Irishman James Joyce, called a "giant of modern literature," how many people has he influenced in the last fifteen years?

This situation, called "influence," is originally a natural phenomenon in a writer's work process, and generally speaking, it is not surprising; but unfortunately, in our society today, the term "influenced" seems to be used too cleverly. Usually, if someone moves a "savage head" from overseas without any alteration, this situation is often called "influenced by such and such a master." In this case, in reality, the term "influence" has lost its original meaning and has become merely a "polite word" for "unconditional imitation."

And this, although only a linguistic embellishment and misunderstanding (or even an error), has a significant impact on the true development of writers. Often, after reading a little of someone's work, one may intentionally or unintentionally imitate it while writing. However, if the non-malicious imitation of unconsciously (or intentionally) writing like someone else due to familiarity with their work is also regarded as being "influenced" by someone, this statement can immediately trap the working writer in a dilemma; thus, Chinese Gorkys, Chinese Chekhovs... one after another, fabricated and immature "domestic products" emerge endlessly.

This is not beneficial to the development of the lauded writer himself.

However, if one is truly influenced by others, it is quite the opposite; not only does it not hinder the writer's development, but it can instead help him to open up his own world and create his own uniqueness. Moreover, as mentioned earlier, a writer's true being influenced by others, even if not necessarily essential, is at least an inevitable phenomenon in his creative process, although it is often not even consciously felt.

Here, it is necessary to point out the difference between genuine "influence" and non-genuine "imitation."

In a lecture titled "My Creative Experience" at the publishing house of the Soviet Trade Union, Alexander Fadeyev said the following:

"If a writer is influenced by others to the point of accepting other writers' ideas and formal techniques, naturally, we call him an Epigonus (i.e., one who completely restates his teacher without creating any new theories). If an artist successfully raises new materials of the present, develops some new ideas, and is influenced by more experienced writers in the learning process, this is not surprising, because he can gradually break away from that influence in the process of development. Undoubtedly, each of us, whoever learns skills from classical writers, must critically study the ideological content of their works and the formal methods of artistic description." (Using the translation by Zhang Zhongshi in "Current Affairs Compilation" Vol. 3, No. 3)

This passage is very useful for us today; it not only points out the difference between influence and imitation (i.e., what is called Epigonus in the text), but also more meaningfully explains the precise method by which writers are "influenced" by others. "Critically studying the ideological content of others' works and the formal methods of artistic description"—this is the "secret" that every writer should know.

And finally, Fadeyev also pointed out that true influence, unlike imitation, which always turns the imitator into a clever "fake," can instead help the writer to create his own characteristics.

"He (the writer) can gradually break away from that influence in the process of development."

There are many examples illustrating this fact: many newcomers influenced by Joyce have developed along their own lines. In the works of Stein, Faulkner, and Hemingway, it is already impossible to find something as lengthy and obscure as "Ulysses"; and who can find the remains of "Resurrection" in "The Rout"?

Only this is truly what can be called "influenced"; and only by truly accepting influence can it be beneficial to the writer.

On Landu Bula Road (Continued and Finished)

— Fei Er

We also stopped the car. We saw that the fallen Indian had been injured: blood was flowing from his face and hands (cut by gravel and thorns!), and his mouth groaned: "Waist pain! Waist pain!" (because when he fell, the cargo and the cart were pressing heavily on his body.)

Several Bengalis opened their companion's mud-stained cargo, distributed his goods, and the other two held him in the middle, pushing three carts parallel to each other. —This injured person was helped up and forced to push the cart, enduring the pain.

"Brave Bengalis! How pitiful, toiling under the pressure of life!" I shouted in my heart.

The car that was holding us also drove away, and I was even more immersed in a tragic scene.

Was it five years ago? I went to Bagan to see a friend from elementary school who was sick. He was being eroded by hemoptysis, and his sunken eye sockets and faint voice proved that his life was coming to an end!

The history of this young friend can be written into a moving novel: after graduating from elementary school, he went to Nanyang (Southeast Asia) to make a living. At that time, it was the golden age of Nanyang. A relative who ran a cloth shop took care of him, having him carry some cloth from the shop every day and go deep into the coconut groves to peddle it to Malay and Chinese women. He also bent his back and shouldered heavy burdens, like a camel, gradually training from carrying hundreds of pounds of goods to being able to carry two or three hundred pounds. Thus, he accumulated a commission to go home to pay off debts and marry a wife. When he came to Nanyang for the second time, he encountered the misfortune of a recession. His relative's shop had already closed, and the goods purchased with cash had no sales. He carried the heavy cargo out early in the morning and returned with it again in the evening. The commission he earned was not enough to cover his own food expenses, and his wife at home had died of an epidemic! Unfortunately, one day, in the dim twilight, he inadvertently fell into a ditch, and his lungs were injured by the cargo. By the time people carried him back, the doctor announced that he was beyond saving.

He died that afternoon, leaving a pot full of blood in the spittoon, which also stained the bed sheets and the underwear on his body. At the time of his death, he was still tightly clutching the red woolen blanket, shouting with all his might:

"My cloth bundle! My cloth bundle!"

Due to the tragedy of the Bengalis, this tragic scene reappeared before my eyes. I heard my twenty-something young friend shout out the cry of human sorrow, and I also saw a large package pressing tightly on the shoulders of many poor people in this world, as if to trample these people like ants under huge feet.

I closed my eyes tightly. I dared not think anymore until the car "beeped" and the driver announced that we had arrived at Landu Bula, and I was awakened and hurriedly got out of the car.

People and Books

— Han Feng

Liu Jingting

Thanks to Wu Weiye's "Biography of Liu Jingting," anyone who dabbles in ancient literature probably knows this famous storyteller. Wu Weiye indeed wrote this character vividly on paper, and Yunting Shanren used him to open the show in "The Peach Blossom Fan," believing that he was "a man of high character and unrestrained spirit, one of us, storytelling is just his extra skill." This storyteller is indeed not an ordinary person, and people often talk about him. Recently, I bought Wang Youding's "Sizhao Tang Collection" and saw two more records about him. One is "Liu Jingting wrote a portrait for Zuo Ningnan, and drew his own image beside it, knowing not to forget, and I praised him for it," with the line "The debater's tongue, the general's sword, when encountering white bones, they are dry and heroic," which can be said to be extremely complimentary to Liu. Wu's biography also mentions Liu's self-portrait, which shows that Jingting not only excelled at storytelling but also could paint. The second is "Four Excellences of Listening to Liu Jingting Telling History," the poem says:

A historian in a hundred years, relying on you to turn sorrow and joy to hurt the soul. No news of Gaozong's crossing south, only seeing the storyteller spreading it.

The events of breaking the enemy are no longer what they were back then, but the portrait of the soldier's power still exists. The bronze pillars of the Three Hans are often joked about, who remembers the general's old iron armor.

Entrusting life and death in a million-strong army, Sun Wu knows this and laughs at talking about war. Spending a thousand gold is commonplace, not exchanging it for the name in the market of Xuyi.

How can a hero's head bow to others, always treating the mountains and rivers as farce. A song about the Jingyang Hill incident, the running water in front of the door, the setting sun in the west (when telling a section of "Water Margin")

This poem certainly reflects the profound sorrow of Prince Yi as a remnant of the previous dynasty. But the moving power of Liu Jingting's storytelling, and that he was not telling stories for no reason, the books he told had their own purpose, is evident here. Yu Danxin's "Banjiao Miscellany" says that "Jingting used Tan Ci, when drunk, struck the table and sang sadly, captivating the audience, like a figure of You Meng and Dongfang Manqian," which is quite sufficient to describe him. It also says: "After Ningnan was defeated, he traveled to the army of Ma, the admiral of Songjiang, and was frustrated, already over eighty years old. Occasionally passing through my residence in Yisui Xuan, he still told the story of Qin Shubao seeing the maiden." This is the history after Wu's biography, which Wu's article did not mention. Zhang Zongzi's "Dream Recollections" is the most vivid and detailed record of the demeanor of storytelling, saying that "his depiction and portrayal are subtle to the finest detail, yet also concise and clean, not verbose, his voice is like a giant bell, when speaking of the crucial points, he shouts and yells, fiercely collapsing the house." And "speaking quietly, his speed, weight, swallowing, and inflection, entering the emotions, entering the muscles and bones, picking the ears of the world's storytellers and making them listen attentively, not fearing that they will bite their tongues and die," which has exhausted the spirit of Jingting's storytelling. In terms of political activities, Wu's biography is the most detailed. Because of proofreading the "Storytelling" article, thinking of "Liu Sheng," I took notes on it.

Debate on Jin Ping

Taking "Jin Ping Mei" as a realistic portrayal of social life of a generation is, generally speaking, a recent event. Therefore, the understanding of this book has changed over the past three hundred years. Recently, when engaging in the study of the history and literature of the period of the Reform Movement, I collected many newspapers and magazines of the time. In "New Novels," I unexpectedly encountered a progressive understanding of "Jin Ping Mei" thirty years ago. One was written by Pingzi, according to the preface, this person was a friend of Liang Qichao, perhaps the master of Pingdeng Ge. His article says: "In the book Jin Ping Mei, the author holds infinite grievances and infinite deep pain, and is in a dark era, with no one to talk to and no way to express it, and has no choice but to use novels to express it. It depicts the social conditions of the time, roughly one class. However, it is different from Water Margin, Water Margin is mostly written in a positive way, Jin Ping is mostly written in a side way; Water Margin is mostly written explicitly, Jin Ping is mostly written implicitly; Water Margin is mostly written in quick words, Jin Ping is mostly written in painful words; Water Margin is clear and cheerful, Jin Ping is hidden and sad; Water Margin holds strange anger, Jin Ping holds strange grievances; the circumstances are different, and the writing is also different. Moreover, the short letters and small songs in it are often outstandingly elegant, surpassing what Song Ci and Yuan Qu can achieve. It can also show the situation of petty people and women at that time, and the degree of people's thinking. It is truly a social novel, and should not be regarded as a pornographic book." Although this view still inevitably has the shortcomings of subjective imagination, its ability to read novels from a social perspective can be said to be the most progressive understanding, looking back thirty years. The second was written by Manshu, who discussed the two books "Jin Ping" and "The Gallant Maid." He said of "Jin Ping" that: "In my opinion, the best chapter titles in novels are in Jin Ping Mei. The reputation of Jin Ping Mei should not be lower than that of Water Margin and Dream of the Red Chamber. This is what novel commentators have called the ancestor of pornographic books. I used to read it, and even after reading several volumes, I still felt no interest. Later, I changed my method and regarded it as a kind of social book to read, and then I realized that there must be something true under the fame. Whoever reads pornographic books, none do not concentrate all their energy on the places where pornography is written, and otherwise, they read casually and do not pay much attention. This is probably the common nature of readers. As for Jin Ping Mei, I certainly cannot say that it is not a pornographic book, but its mystery is definitely not in the writing of pornography, because this book is a book that depicts the lower-class women's society. Commentators say that Dream of the Red Chamber is completely taken from Jin Ping Mei, and is said to be an inverted image of Jin Ping Mei, which should be true. If its chapter titles and inscriptions are truly excellent." Although his views are not as good as Pingzi's, he can indeed make a further observation on Jin Ping. This Manshu is also a friend of Yin Bing, I wonder if it is Su Manshu? I hope that Manshu's friends can verify this.

Moving House

— Li Huiying

When Ya Ru and I came to Shanghai, we lived in one room, and we always felt that there were too few things and that we lacked utensils. Moreover, living together, we gradually felt a bit bland. At that time, I thought: I should slowly make some odd items, such as a writing desk, rattan chairs, a kettle, tea sets, a vase, a trunk, etc., partly for my own use, and partly to decorate the room a little. If people say that life is bland, I might as well bring my mother out to add an old person, which will definitely eliminate some of the dryness in life.

At that time, we lived on Rue du Père Robert. In three months, we had to move because the original house was too dilapidated, and the newly rented house was both new and cheap. The new address was Route Frelaut. At that time, because there were few things, a total of three rickshaws, including the people, were enough to move everything.

After that, we moved from Route Frelaut to Avenue du Roi Albert, Avenue Haig, and after several moves, we still did not feel much difficulty in moving because our things had not increased much. However, time slowly passed, and Ya Ru and I had been living together for two years. In addition to the two of us, there was actually a child; it was no longer the bland state of life before. A little person, noisy all day long. At the same time, there were also many more daily necessities: beds, tables, chairs, desks, boxes, cradles, and some odd items, two or three times more than before. However, living in habit every day, I had not noticed these extra items until recently when we had to move again, and the problem also arose.

In advance, I discussed with Ya Ru the method of hiring a car. At least eight or nine rickshaws were needed, and to Xujiahui, each car would cost at least thirty cents, plus the tip, three dollars would be reliable, which was not worthwhile. Hiring a small car, about three would be enough, but the price of a small car was high, each would cost ninety cents to one dollar, and people had to follow, which was not worthwhile. What to do? Now we really hate that we have too many things. Moreover, Ya Ru actually said:

"Usually, I told you to buy fewer utensils, but you wouldn't listen. What's the matter? Now you know it's troublesome, right?"

What she said was actually wrong. The wrong thing was that she shouldn't have put the responsibility for having too many things on me. Honestly, some of the things were what she told me to buy. What should I say to her? Argue? It was useless, and even her complaint was of no help.

"What's the point of saying these things? Just think of a way to move," I finally replied to her. At the same time, I seemed to think that I shouldn't be scolded for nothing, and then said, "But when moving, didn't you often say that there were too few things to use?"

Finally, we decided to hire a moving truck because since such a truck could move both people and things, wouldn't it be very fast to go?

"How annoying, moving house, what a troublesome thing."

Ya Ru was complaining while packing things. The child was also making a fuss, making it so that you could not only not do more things, but also messed up your mood.

"How could I not know that moving house is troublesome?"

I said, continuing to pack things. A cloud of dust rose in the room, and some torn paper, broken shoes, and ink bottles lay messily on the floor.

Why don't we move? Why should we be afraid of trouble? Thirteen dollars a month for rent, the amount is not small. Now that we move to Xujiahui, the subtenant there is an old friend of many years, the rent is less, and when we are short of money, we can still owe it. Where can we find such a convenient thing?

"Isn't it that after moving, we will have some advantages, convenient places?" I stopped and said to Ya Ru, "How come, have you forgotten what I said to you?"

That day, we finally moved both people and things over. We hope that the words "moving house" will not reappear in our lives.

Toward Evening (12)

— Qu Yi

The drinking and eating began. Among the four people, except for the author of National Literature Spectacle, who, holding his smoking paraphernalia, refrained from drinking a drop due to harming the national economy, the three people were almost swigging from jars and urns. They were all together. They drank one cup after another, and they talked even more about one thing after another. When they talked about something they agreed on, the uncle and nephew would nod their heads in unison:

"No need to say, no need to say." The nephew shook his head and sighed, but still seemed somewhat calm. "I've said it before. What comes in from the counter is still more than what goes out from the drawer. There are more beggars at the door than buyers. Expenses are inevitable, and the scene must be set. Upward! Ha, upward. Those who do business can't blame the upward trend. But I don't blame myself either. It's interesting to talk about it. From the time Dad died until now, the money wasn't all spent by me. It's fate. If you say I don't know how to do business, I can still read the wind and steer the rudder. But for six or seven years, it's always—always—always the same, a 'sigh' character. Only that year, the year when Ning and Han split the family, did I have a stroke of luck. Old, outdated things were also sold as new trendy goods. Something worth a dime would sell for two dollars, or even more than ten dollars—that year was, was—um, what about the second year? Um! No need to say, no need to say, come on! Have another drink? Have another drink!"

"Can I still drink?" Black Eyebrows straightened up. The cucumber face split open another crack. The cups were raised in unison, "Then you—sigh! You, Mr. Li! Come on! Let's have another drink!"

Drinking sullenly, without speaking. Li An was already a bit tipsy. But he also accepted a big cup with a smile.

"Good! Happy! Happy! I'll come to your wedding feast in the future!" Hu Yiyuan looked at Li An's demeanor, raised his cup and touched Li An's cup, and said, "Poor little fellow, he hasn't even hung a name in the Women's Army yet, let alone been a small soldier?"

Supplement to the Shanghai Newspaper

L>Random Talk

International Anti-War Strike Movement

— Qiong Sheng

A dispatch from New York states: 100,000 American university students who believe in "freedom" are showing signs of a strike movement to oppose the tendency of nationalism and the militarist attitude in some aspects within the country, due to the existence of "various forces in the United States that are currently forcing the country into war and pan-aggressive tendencies." Furthermore, similar student movements are also taking place in countries such as Canada, Cuba, Argentina, and Chile. Students from other countries who approve of the student anti-war conference plan are all invited to participate in this international strike movement.

Of course, to a certain extent, this movement takes the anti-nationalism and pan-aggressive tendencies it proclaims as its goal. After Hitler and Mussolini are declaring that all students nationwide must receive military training, this cannot but be said to be an event where "public reason resides in people's hearts." This is like how, after the outbreak of the European War, the student circles in Beijing rose up to oppose participation in the war, at least it can make some people who have been drinking Yangzhou rice soup of "patriotism" from the powers that be, and who have inexplicably walked into war, awaken.

Regarding the matter of war, everyone now knows that it is to sacrifice the majority of people for the benefit of a small number, and if people recognize this reality, it will be difficult to maintain this deception. Obviously, this deception has learned a historical lesson in the European War. On the one hand, bones were exposed in the battlefield, creating many orphans and widows, and on the other hand, entertainment and revelry were rampant, not to mention that the glory and "justice" of the motherland that was fought for were only a continuation of the exploitation of slaves. The anti-war movement that has been growing since the end of the European War is due to the exposure of this deception.

Therefore, no matter how loudly Hitler shouts about restoring the Third Reich, and how highly Mussolini's sermons about the glory of the Roman Empire are sung, the general public, looking back on the past, still cannot erase the traces of their blood-stained wounds. But they are nationally unified and claim to be prosperous, why are they able to do this? "Pan-isms." Pan-isms can be said to be the Italian army going to Africa to conquer colonies, and pan-isms can also make the people of Saar declare the victory of the "nation" under the coercion of the "German front." Especially in the present time of tight war crisis, pan-isms have almost become a popular weapon of preparedness in various countries.

But this kind of "militarist attitude" of pan-isms can temporarily push humanity towards war, and at the same time, it can also push them towards opposing war. The rise of the international anti-war strike movement is a sign that students who believe in "freedom" have realized that war will not only not benefit them, but will also be extremely harmful. It is very clear: if you want to "love your country," this patriotism is not for the majority of the people, but for yourself. We certainly cannot hope that this strike movement will cause many "militarist attitudes" that are eager to gain victory in war to change, but to be able to make them change, only some people who are facing each other in the trenches because of "patriotism" must feel that their enemies are not these "soldiers," but others.

The anti-war strike movement should have this enlightenment for people.

Song of the Condemned

— Qin Jian

(Bare tree branches and small grasses begin to reveal hints of tender green amidst the brown and black, and wild sparrows are also busily planning new days in the sun. People can hardly fail to notice: another spring has arrived!

Warm air currents, warm breezes, intertwine to weave a series of strikingly discordant, almost unbearable days; good scenery and bad moods stubbornly confront each other in my heart, and I am as disoriented as a kite caught in a whirlwind.

——Oh, this endless chain of days!

However, now it is: this chain is pulling the green spring along with it.)

A strange hot wind blew in through the window,

Page 20

and my heart involuntarily trembled; then I jumped up in surprise: it is another new, unfamiliar spring!

I glanced at my reflection in the large mirror: all the signs of a life devoid of joy were fully present, the graying stars in my temples, the hard lines of life on my face, and the dimness in my eyes, devoid of spirit.

I felt the chain of days like a giant African python, tightening its coils around my entire life day by day; I was bound like a condemned prisoner before the guillotine.

What I felt was heavy suffocation: the shackles of days are terrifying, the shackles of days are stubborn.

So, desolately accompanying the trembling six-stringed zither, I began to sing softly: "Before the small grass of spring, I am a condemned man in a chain gang…"

The sound, like a wavering ripple in the blue water, drifted leisurely into the fields outside the window; in the zither's coda, clouds drifted slowly in the sky: one piece, two pieces…

Countless youthful days were all transformed in the unfamiliar cloud mountains of foreign lands, teaching me the ways of a condemned man with precious treasures from many books, and the vitality of stubborn youth: so in the inevitable conflict between generations, braving the white-hot flames, I drifted away, leaving the sighs of the elderly behind without emotion.

Some magnificent spectacles were arranged head-on in the world ahead: terror, humiliation, hunger, and instability, like snowflakes in the north wind, followed endless days, pelting towards me like beads.

I also drew courage and comfort from my own and others' worlds; the hardships of life are not worth worrying about, they are the forging and testing of young people, valuable night lights on the long journey of life.

Firmly remembering these precious words, I silently bore the heavy burden of the world, walking past with rough steps like a camel.

It was as if every day I was playing hide-and-seek with those future days while dragging heavy shackles, I hid, I escaped, and so the days flowed by like water. Every spring, when a new group of days began, I inevitably felt a burst of heat, a burst of anxiety. In the end, the beautiful spark of hope withered along with the youthful light in my eyes, and I grew old in the sorrows of life, and then I began to understand: "I am a condemned man in a chain gang."

So, I lived on so calmly: the condemned man has his certain way of life, there is no way to relieve the tribulations of life.

And now it is: the black hair is also dotted with white stars in the desolate large mirror; knowing that it is not clever to envy the green in the pile of withered grass; so when the oriole sings proudly on the branch opposite the window, I cannot concede and put the noise of the condemned man into the trembling of the six-stringed zither:

"Before the small grass of spring, I am a condemned man in a chain gang."

Decline

— Ya Fei

The owner of Yuan Kee Store, Second Master, sat at a south-facing desk, flipping through the ledger page by page with his left hand; his right hand snapped and crackled as he worked the abacus beads. He carefully watched the numbers on the abacus, but his face was covered with a layer of frost-like melancholy. His two hands trembled slightly, and a pair of lifeless eyes peered out from under his old copper-framed glasses, casting glances of annoyance towards the street in front of the store. But the street was cold and deserted, almost like you could catch ghosts there. He moved his gaze to the counter, and immediately saw the apprentice, Ah Cai, dozing off on it.

"Ah Cai, didn't you get enough sleep last night? Dozing off in broad daylight, no wonder all the business has been driven away!" He seemed to think that the store's poor business was entirely due to Ah Cai's dozing off, so he had to vent his anger on him. Ah Cai, scolded by him, hurriedly rubbed his dark hands over his eyes, drawing a blurry gray circle around them, and trembled like a small mouse into the corner of the counter.

"Sigh! It's really hard to do business these days. The accounts for the upstream suppliers can't be shorted by half a cent, not even for a moment, but the retail business is so slow, and only 30% of the accounts owed by the villages are being collected. The store is out of goods, but where has the money gone? What kind of store is it if you open the door and have nothing to sell? And there's no money to replenish the goods! Moreover, the suppliers have declared that they only deal in cash this year. If you don't offer credit, no business comes to the door, but if you offer it, you can't get the money back. It's really hard, hard!" As soon as he thought of "hard," it seemed as if countless "hard" characters appeared in his mind; even as if his surroundings were all "hard" characters. He saw "hard" characters everywhere on the abacus and in the ledger! He was a little frightened, and suddenly threw the "General Clearance" ledger of Yuan Kee Store angrily on the ground, and with a crackling sound, he messed up all the numbers that had been calculated on the abacus; patting his head, he took a cold breath, stood up abruptly, then stepped down from behind the desk, glancing angrily towards the door, muttering to himself:

"Damn it, I don't want to run this lousy store anymore!"

He picked up a water pipe, and Ah Cai hurriedly and carefully put a lit paper on it. While he smoked, he was pondering the question of closing or keeping the store open. He thought that in the first year that Yuan Kee Store was opened, after deducting all expenses, there was still a surplus of more than four hundred dollars at the end of the year. In the second year, his wife had a serious illness, and then she died; so the store was basically working for nothing, with no extra money. Last year, the third year, was even worse, with losses, expenses, consumption, and debts, and now the store's total inventory is less than two hundred dollars. Moreover, last year, in order to repay the debt to the rice store, he borrowed fifty dollars from Jin Sheng, with a monthly interest of five silver dollars. He had originally planned to repay him after the market opened on the fifth day of the new year, but nearly a month has passed, and there is less than twenty dollars in business, and the store's goods must be replenished, what to do! Thinking of this, his mind became even more confused, he simply could not think any further. He put the water pipe down in his hand, already stopping smoking.

"Close it down!" After being stunned for a long time, he discussed with himself: "No, if I close the door, it will be even more difficult to collect the rural debts, and they will have an even better excuse to delay. But if I don't close it, I'll just have to watch it lose money; there's no business, I don't dare to offer credit, there's no money to replenish the goods, sigh!" This problem was really difficult to solve; he couldn't close it, and he couldn't keep it open, and no one wanted to take it over. Thinking about it again and again, it was still like tangled hemp, making his heart ache. Finally, he simply put the water pipe on the desk and stopped smoking.

He sat on a sugar jar lid, hugged his knees with both hands, and stared blankly outside the door. In those two hours, not a single customer came to the counter. Although a few people walked past the door, in his eyes, they were all annoying faces and blurry shadows, and the street was completely silent.

"Hard!" So again, countless "hard" characters swirled in his mind!

Father

— Dai Ni

Spring brings the gentle breeze of February:

In the lonely small building in the thick fog—as if in a monastery, the alarm clock rang at six o'clock, and the father, whose hair was mottled with mental illness, sat up in bed, stretching his stiffening limbs. This slight tremor awakened his son from his beautiful dream, a tall young man with a pair of arms like a thousand pounds.

"Dad, don't always pay attention to those flowers, it's not even light yet."

"Yes. —Today is the tenth anniversary of your mother's death, I want to go to the cemetery."

Dad spoke with a heavy, slurred tongue. From his prematurely aged face, the majesty of a forty-five-year-old man could no longer be found. He got out of bed slowly, put on his morning coat, and went to the clothes tree covered with a faded embroidered sheet, pulling out a set of outdated, slightly worn Western clothes, carefully dressing himself like a groom going to church to get married, and finally had his son button on a colorful tie, then walked alone into the courtyard.

The son quickly finished getting ready, took a brocade purse and a rattan cane from beside his father's pillow. He jumped to the stone steps in the courtyard, where his father was holding the potted flowers under the eaves of the railing and taking them to the wall that was shone by the sun every day.

"Dad, let me help you move them"!

Usually Dad would shake his head and say, "No! No! I've moved them for many years and never broken a pot"! He would tremble like that, carrying the potted flowers back and forth, and would get very angry if his son didn't listen to him. —Today he didn't answer, looking up at the sky: the thick fog was gradually dissipating, and the sunlight hidden in it was dazzling his eyes, or perhaps he was particularly excited, he also felt a little uncomfortable, coughed, and sat down on the stone steps. The son then lifted up two of them with both hands.

"Be careful, don't break them! Your mother cherished these few pots of flowers the most"!

His voice was as gentle as motherly love.

As they opened the small gate of the courtyard, the ringing of a milk delivery bicycle faded away on the stone path. Dad held a bouquet of flowers in one hand, supported himself with the rattan cane, and walked forward with quick steps, his son following closely behind him, not daring to support him.

The sound of two mismatched leather shoes echoed on the stone path, like grand music in the clear morning breeze, two leaping hearts, the colorful tie fluttering on Dad's shoulder.

The keeper of the cemetery was a sharp-eyed old man, who stopped sweeping with his long-handled broom and said:

"I knew the old gentleman would be coming today."

"We've both grown a year older, but you're still so healthy." As if he were a young man, he patted the old man's shoulder, but felt as if his own leg strength was not enough and took two steps back.

"Hehe," he laughed unnaturally, "a distant ten years!"

Almost mumbling, they walked toward the tomb path, again so quickly.

The son was a head taller than him; standing side by side in front of the tombstone of "Deceased Wife ×××," his head sank to his chest, and he

Page 21

prayed in his heart: "Ten years, I have cherished those flowers you loved as if loving a young girl! Do you see your son, he has also reached the age for his father to marry"?

He felt that he had handed over a heavy responsibility. He straightened his colorful tie, which had been blown up, and gazed at the tiny flowers nodding to him in the gentle breeze of February.

Clouds and Sky Leaving Hometown

— Ren Ying

"Since parting, I recall our meeting, how many times have our souls dreamed together. Tonight I still hold the silver lamp to illuminate, I still fear that our meeting is but a dream!"

On the way back and forth through life, in the autumn of a foreign land; I long for the clouds and sky of my hometown. In the season of yellow flowers, the southern gentle breeze blew her to the bustling Shanghai. A three-day stay, immersed in ancient dreams. Hastily, we are again on the road back to our hometown.

But alas, like a midnight dream! These old traces have again turned into bubbles! Facing the long sky of the city, I long for the clouds and sky of my hometown. Seeing the faded spring light, my heart is like a solitary goose leaving the flock! A pang of bitterness fills my heart.

Recalling the old outlines, only confusion! The water in the big Jia River carries a joyful heart, and also carries a sorrowful body. Once or twice a year, her pain intensifies. My hometown is also decaying year by year along with the ancient city walls! Like a kite with a broken string, without boundaries. Like a spotted eagle with an arrow, reflecting bloodstains.

In the south-facing window, the faint sunlight of autumn is reflected. In a joyful atmosphere, I read every magazine brought from Shanghai. In the neat drawer, I select a note card and send it to a friend under the red lanterns. Praising my hometown, it is always like being in the embrace of the spring breeze. The pastoral interests attract my dissolute heart. Closing the book and pondering, her face is a manifestation of optimism.

In the backyard, goldfish swim in the calm water. Sticking together in pairs, like mandarin ducks side by side. The chrysanthemums in the flower bed unfold their mature, tender yellow. A gust of hollow autumn wind causes the old banyan tree to rustle. Burning a cigarette, I meditate in the shadow of the setting sun.

This painting of my hometown's outline is fading away with the passing of time! Longing for the clouds and sky of my hometown, infinite sorrow attacks my body and mind.

It's all because Emperor Qianlong visited Jiangnan three times, leaving historical sites in Suzhou. Therefore, it has been a provincial capital since ancient times. The censorate is established in Suzhou. Endless scenery to talk about leisurely.

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Film Special

A Brief History of Film Development (7)

— Wen Ying

(7) The Beginning of Hollywood's Founding

Today, whenever anyone mentions the word "Hollywood," they almost certainly mean "cinema." Hollywood and cinema have become almost inseparable. But strangely, the films we've discussed so far all happened before cinema moved to Hollywood. Now we'll talk about the origins of Hollywood.

The invention of Hollywood, like the invention of cinema, was an accident. In 1913, when the film industry was just beginning to flourish, major film companies and figures in the film industry were concentrated or scattered in cities such as New York, Shika Valley, Wakelan, and Philadelphia. There were also a few small film companies in Los Angeles, but in that small village called Hollywood, people rarely saw a camera, unless filmmakers from Los Angeles occasionally went there to shoot outdoor scenes.

"Holly" is originally a thorny shrub with uneven, prickly leaves. In winter, its leaves remain evergreen and glossy, and small red berries grow in the middle of the leaves, like the red berries of Nandina domestica. It is used to make Christmas wreaths. Hollywood was named because of the holly groves that grew there. At that time, Hollywood was just a real estate name, but those who discovered that Hollywood could be used as a residential area have now become millionaires.

Among those people, one who was directly related to the invention of Hollywood was Robert Brunton. Brunton was a Scotsman who worked as a set designer, painter, and carpenter in a film company. He came to America with the famous British actor, Sir Henry Irving. But later he became interested in film and did not return with him. However, he soon became unemployed because he had a bad temper and lived day to day without a plan. One day he went out for a walk and reached the current Sunset Boulevard. He stopped. He saw a large area of wasteland with only a few shack-like houses. He remembered reading in the newspaper that a newly established film company was moving to Los Angeles but had not yet found a suitable location.

Can you guess who those founders of the new company were? They were Jesse Lasky, who was half-poor and half-rich, Samuel Goldfish ("Goldfish," who later changed his name to Samuel Goldwyn), and Arthur Friend, a poor lawyer. These people pooled their limited funds to start a film company and hired a down-on-his-luck writer named Cecil B. DeMille as their director and stage manager. At that time, Dustin Farnum was just beginning to gain some small fame on the stage. They hired him to make a film.

Brunton thought of this and immediately ran to the Alexandria Hotel in Los Angeles to see Goldwyn. People at that time spoke less and did more. Brunton met Goldwyn and started by saying, "I've found you the best possible location." Goldwyn was also not one for much talk. He simply asked, "Is the land expensive?" That's how Hollywood was created.

The price of that wasteland and a few wooden houses was very limited—only a few hundred dollars per acre—and the deal was closed in a few weeks. The new company was called Lasky Studio. This company later created countless stars, such as Wallace Reid, Gloria Swanson, Bebe Daniels, Dorothy Dalton, and so on, but those are just a few of the most famous. But at the time, when the founders started working in a few wooden houses, how could they have foreseen the greatness of their future endeavors?

The success of the Lasky Company gradually attracted the attention of film figures from other places, and everyone began to move to Hollywood. Hollywood's ability to become the film capital of the world also had to do with favorable timing and location. The climate in Southern California is mild and spring-like all year round. Sunlight, the only thing needed at that time because they rarely used lights and relied on sunlight to shoot films, was particularly bright in Hollywood, with very little rain throughout the year. In terms of location, the price of land in Hollywood was very cheap. The price of one acre of land in New York could buy dozens of acres in Hollywood. There were many wooden houses there, and the price of wood was very low, making the cost of building studios very small. Labor costs were only half of what they were in New York. With so many advantages, Hollywood's future development was a natural fit. (To be continued)

Film Reviews

Review of "King of the Ritz"

— Ling He

King of the Ritz — Carlton

Recently, we have seen few British films. The "King of the Ritz," which is now showing at the Carlton, appears in the form of a satirical comedy.

It doesn't lose its comedic effect. Its style, like many British comedies, is never too frivolous, like American slapstick films. Instead, it maintains the consistent solemnity of the British, carrying a strong sense of gentlemanliness, as people generally say, even in scenes that are meant to be funny. This aspect should be unique to British films. However, perhaps because of this reason, British films are not enthusiastically welcomed by people who are used to watching American films, although this does not negate their value in cinematic art.

"King of the Ritz" is not without value, at least the screenwriter's attempt; not teaching the little clerk leader of the hotel to climb up, let him awaken the spring dream of wealth, still return to the original place, still combine with the same status of the maid, is still more desirable. Similarly, the screenwriter makes the kings go back sadly, the vain rich widow also finally combines with the golf player, each returns to its original position, and walks out of the door of the magnificent hotel. But the screenwriter did not succeed in the main reality, at least not in the great achievement in technology.

Perhaps people see the emperor with many medals in his pocket, and he can confer them on people at any time as he pleases. Perhaps people find the ugliness of that group of luxurious men and women, such as the dance teacher, such as the golfer athlete, such as the flirtatious widow, such as the emperor's entourage, etc., very interesting as satire, but this includes a lot of unrealistic expressions. The most obvious is that the hotel waiter happens to be the Marquis, and the various things of the male protagonist in the Marquis's mansion are unbelievable, although these places can fully make people laugh.

Because Stanley Luoino's acting is very good, in the last scene of the Marquis's official residence, the drunken singing is very emotional, and this tragic part of the comedy does have some value. Like the female lead's licentiousness and vanity, and the king's flirting, the time the three men visit the widow at the same time, is also an excellent skill

However, in general, the lack of success in this film is that it is not technically enough to express the theme, so that it has always become a mediocre comedy.

Abfuess Schalomoff's New Work "Incense Seal Illusion" to be Performed

Russian composer Abfuess Schalomoff has resided in Tianjin and Beijing for over a decade, devoting himself to the study of Chinese music and drama and seeking ways to improve Chinese music and drama. Schalomoff believes that Chinese music has a wealth of melodies, and if composers extract its essence and use methods such as harmony and counterpoint to create symphonic works, then Chinese music can also stand out in the world of music and rival the advanced countries of the West. Schalomoff advocates starting with music to reform Chinese drama, as Chinese drama is similar to Western opera and must have special music suitable for the plot in order to avoid the disease of repetition. Schalomoff wanted to realize his dream, so he composed an opera performed in the United States, which was well received by the people there. His symphony and pantomime "The Heart of the Piano in Rippling Light" was performed in Shanghai the year before last, and critics called it the harbinger of improved Chinese drama. Schalomoff has recently composed a pantomime called "Incense Seal Illusion," which is divided into three acts. The plot is bizarre, the music is beautiful, and the performers are all Chinese actors with rich experience and well-known reputations. It is directed by Xu Jichuan and Yang Yulou, and is now fully rehearsed. It is scheduled to be performed at the Carlton Theatre starting on the 13th of this month, for three consecutive days. The scenery of the play was painted by Dong Lachiff, a professor at the Hangzhou National Academy of Art. The music is performed by the entire Shanghai Municipal Council String Orchestra, conducted by Mei Baiqi. Those who wish to listen to elegant music and use Schalomoff's work as a reference for studying and improving Chinese drama should not miss this opportunity. Seats can be reserved at Robinson Piano Shop, 78 Nanjing Road.

Chen Yan and Zhang Zhenduo in Tianyi's new film "Returning Home".

Many Actors in "Falling Flower Season"

"Falling Flower Season" Our volunteer army is fiercely resisting the Japanese army, and it is "Falling Flower Season" again. Our volunteer army finally retreats to a village backed by mountains and facing water due to lack of supplies and equipment. Some of them drifted to the city, where they lead painful occupational lives: some work as railway workers amid the wailing of steam whistles, some work as sanitation workers on desolate early morning streets, some sell sesame cakes and fried dough sticks in huge windstorms and rain, some build roads under the scorching sun... "Falling Flower Season" is directed by Wu Cun and stars Xu Lai, Wang Xianzai, Zhao Dan, Gu Meijun, Gu Lanjun, Mei Xi, etc. There are vast scenes and more than a thousand actors.

Small News

— Wen

Zhang Shichuan led photographer Chen Chen and over twenty others to Nanchang the day before yesterday to shoot newsreels. They will stay for about a week and then return.

Xue Lingxian, who was once rumored to have died, will return to Shanghai from Hong Kong this month.

Cao Xisong is currently writing the script for "The Love History of Mr. Wang" and plans to send the script to Beijing for review.

It is rumored that Gao Lihan will join Lian Er.

Yi Hua's new film "The Beginning of Man" is half finished.

Film Novel

Schoolgirl's Loving Mother (Grand Old Girl) (8)

— Shu Min

Dade hurriedly pretended to be indifferent and replied, "It's nothing." He folded the newspaper and stuffed it behind his back, saying repeatedly, "It's nothing." Miss Beales, like a teacher scolding a cheating student, stretched out her hand and said, "Give it to me!" Dade reluctantly handed over the newspaper and said, "Miss Beales, now is not the time to read the newspaper. Why don't you wait until..." But Miss Beales had already seen that piece of news... She was suspended from the Education Bureau... but not under the name of suspension, but under the name of long-term leave... and her successor had already been appointed. She was stunned when she saw it. Her lips trembled, but she couldn't say anything.

Dade carefully looked at her face and said, "Miss Beales, go inside and sit down." Beales still forced a smile and said, "No, Clarence. I'm fine." Dade comforted her and said, "Long-term leave... can't you still do something?" Beales said, "I don't know how to do anything." Dade suddenly became afraid for her. He stared at her and asked, "Miss Beales, have they arranged anything for you... I'm talking about money? Don't you have a pension?" Miss Beales looked ahead and sighed, "I have to work for forty years to get a pension. Now, it's only thirty-eight years. It's a pity I'm too young." She laughed, laughing in a strange voice. She gently patted Dade's hand twice and quietly walked away.

Dade also felt sad for her. Seeing her walk away, he said to himself, "Too young..." His eyes looked at the newspaper again, now looking at a piece of news about the President. He suddenly had an idea... He thought of his classmate from his childhood, the "little girl"! He shrugged his shoulders, straightened his chest, and made a resolute expression.

The next afternoon, Gilly ran to the principal's office to see Miss Beales. She had tears on her face, and when the principal stretched out her arms and hugged her, Miss Beales patted Gilly's golden head and said, "Gilly, it's okay." Gilly cried, "This is so unfair... I argued with my father for a long time... but he wouldn't listen to me at all... He said that the matter has come to this point and cannot be changed... Miss Beales, what should I do?" Beales said, "Don't worry about me... I'm not worth anything... I'm old... everything is over, but you... you're just starting... you have a long future... Gilly, do you know? You are a talented person... a genius." Gilly kissed Miss Beales's dry cheek and said, "No matter what happens in the future, I will never do anything to hurt you again... ever and ever." She said, and walked away with a bag of tears.

Outside the school gate, Sandy sat in his truck, anxiously watching the school gate from time to time. After a while, Gilly came out. Sandy jumped out of the truck, helped Gilly into the truck, and jumped in himself, sitting beside her. Gilly's hand reached into Sandy's hand. She looked at Sandy with tears in her eyes and whispered, "Sandy, from now on, I will never pretend again." Sandy looked at her and said softly, "I know, you will never pretend again." He reached out one hand to hold Gilly's waist, and the other hand drove the car away.

The last moment is the saddest moment. The new principal had already come to discuss how to take over things. Although Melis was a little reluctant to part with the old principal, she couldn't do anything about the issue of the rice bowl. But Boz had walked away in anger to pack his things. Finally, Miss Beales was left alone in the principal's office. Peace... peace after the pain... but there was no hope anymore. He looked at a wooden plaque hanging on the wall, which was embossed with the words: "Do what is right - courage." She couldn't help but lower her head, and she couldn't stop the tears from welling up in her eyes, even though she closed her eyes tightly. (To be continued)
